Current Affairs Commentary

The New Trend of the Banking Industry in Our Country

— Yan

Since the financial panic of last year, many commercial banks in our country have narrowed their scope. Recently, there has been a new trend in the way they lend money and organize themselves.

Commercial banks' lending to industry and commerce has long been difficult due to the decline of industry and commerce in recent years. In speculation, it is difficult to seek favorable development after currency management. Under these circumstances, in order to reduce the responsibility for lending, banks strive to diversify the amount of capital used. The target of lending has shifted from industry and commerce to rural areas and government construction projects. The recent organization of Jiangsu and Zhejiang spring cocoon syndicates, fishing industry syndicates, etc. is one example.

As for the organization of banks, it is gradually shifting from dispersion to concentration. Commercial banks have been increasing rapidly in the past few years, but the weakness of their strength and the dispersion of talents are unavoidable. The recent trend is that banks with similar characteristics, such as Zhonghui and Jiangsu-Zhejiang Bank, Jiangsu and Silk Industry Bank, are merging. Although it is impossible to know how the business will be conducted after the merger, it is commendable in terms of concentrating strength.

Lending targets are tending towards rural areas and national construction projects, which is of course correct from the perspective of the national economy. But what should be noted is that it is difficult to easily talk about investment in today's industrial and commercial decline. However, the decline of industry and commerce is due to the environment. Therefore, how to use strength to help industry and commerce struggle out of the darkness is still a part of the responsibility of financiers. Regarding lending to rural areas or agricultural products, we believe that lenders should also pay attention to the commercial environment. In the past, silk and tea loans often caused the abuse of excessive lending. As a result, agricultural product prices plummeted, putting farmers and themselves in an unfavorable position. As for assisting government construction projects, although the interest is still passed on to the general public, it is of course different from the heavy exploitation of public bonds in previous years.

After the merger of commercial banks, their strength will be increased, and their business development plans will be easier to implement. We have two small hopes for the subsequent business plans of these banks. (1) Each bank in the group should preferably identify its own target and do it separately. In this way, the division of labor will be meticulous, and observation can be thorough. (2) In the past, many commercial banks were mostly concentrated in a corner of Shanghai due to the limitation of funds when they were established, forming a unique expansion of urban finance. After the merger, if it is impossible to get rid of the city due to various relationships, it is hoped that more strength will be distributed to the inland to fulfill the responsibility of regulating finance.

Bai Chongxi Attempts to Seize Guangdong Territory

(Hong Kong) Bai Chongxi is taking advantage of the internal disintegration of the Guangdong army to try to seize Guangdong territory, and temporarily takes a defensive position against Hunan and Guizhou. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) It is rumored that Li Zongren is still at Hekou in Sanshui and has not returned to Guangxi, with the intention of leading the Guangxi army eastward to seize Guangdong. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Deng E, the captain of the armored train team, and Ren Fei, the deputy captain, led the team to Hong Kong on the afternoon of the 18th. Twelve tanks and eight armored vehicles were left unattended. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Lower-ranking officers and soldiers of the Guangdong army unanimously oppose the Guangxi army's eastward movement, because the Guangxi army will be issued military pay and equipment as soon as they arrive in Guangdong, while the Guangdong army has been in arrears for three months and has not received a single cent. There is also a unanimous expression to welcome Yu Hanmou. Many believe that Yu can arrive in Guangdong within three days. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Chen Jitang's Resignation and Departure from Guangdong

(Hong Kong) After the 2nd, 3rd, and 5th Armies of the Guangdong army opposed the war and Huang Guangrui and others led the entire air force team and pilots to leave the province, the situation in Guangdong and Guangxi suddenly disintegrated. At the same time, he received a telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek on the 18th, which showed great care and concern, which was quite moving. He then decided to implement his resignation and return political power to the Central Government. At 10:00 AM on the 18th, he convened a meeting at the headquarters and announced his intention to leave Guangdong. All the generals expressed their approval. At 12:00 PM, he summoned Li Yangjing, Miao Peinan, Lin Yizhong, Ou Fangpu, Lin Shiqing, Du Yiqian, He Luo, Li Shuzong and other confidants at the Yantang Military Academy to discuss how to handle the aftermath. (1) All troops in the northeast and two rivers and garrisoned in the provincial capital were handed over to Li Yangjing and Miao Peinan for unified leadership. (2) The security of the provincial capital was handed over to Li Shuzong, the commander of the Gendarmerie, and He Luo, the director of the Public Security Bureau, to be responsible for maintaining it. (3) In terms of politics, it was divided into Lin Yizhong, Ou Fangpu, and Huang Linshu to temporarily maintain the status quo. When Yu Hanmou arrived in the provincial capital, he would properly transfer them separately. He drafted a telegram to Yu Hanmou, expressing his imminent departure from Guangdong. The original text of the telegram has been seen in yesterday's telegram. After the meeting, Chen returned to the headquarters to finish unfinished military affairs, and summoned senior personnel to make a farewell speech for half an hour. The content is unknown. Li left, Chen returned to his private residence in Meihua Village to rest for a while, around 4:00 PM. Lin Yizhong and others rushed to meet with him again to talk about everything. At 4:45 PM, Li was refused by the Guangxi army in the Xicun area of Huangsha, and failed to seize Guangzhou City. All the plans failed. He then took the Southwest Civil Aviation plane back to Guangxi. The tense situation in the provincial capital gradually eased. Chen Jitang was able to take Chen Weizhou and more than a dozen guards by car from his residence to the Yuzhu Fortress at 5:05 PM, boarded the Haihu warship and drifted eastward. Goodbye Guangzhou. Only a few people, including Lin Yizhong, came to the dock to see him off, and they faced each other sadly. The ship sailed to Huangpu and stopped. Around 9:00 PM, Chen changed to a British ship to Hong Kong. It was originally planned to arrive at the port at 3:00 AM on the 19th. However, a strong wind and rain made the journey very slow, and it was delayed until 7:00 AM to enter the port. The Hong Kong Police Department sent more than 30 detectives, divided into police boats to escort them. More than 20 Chinese and foreign reporters also drove electric boats to wait on the sea. At 7:20 AM, the ship berthed on the Tsim Sha Tsui sea. Chen and others changed to a small boat opened by his family to meet him, leaned against the Taikoo Wharf, and boarded the shore in the wind and rain. They took a car straight back to the private residence on Fenghui Terrace to rest. Chen did not meet with reporters due to physical discomfort, and no written statement was released. (19th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Financial authorities are now planning to take advantage of the military and political reforms in Guangdong Province to thoroughly reorganize the currency system in Guangdong Province without harming the social economy and the people's livelihood, so as to avoid the people of Guangdong from falling into an irretrievable place. It is reported that the responsible personnel of the three major banks of the Central Government, China, and Communications came to Beijing a few days ago to take advantage of the convenience of a certain senior official in Guangdong Province to discuss ways to solve this problem. A complete result has been obtained. The reorganization of the Guangdong currency system this time can be carried out smoothly, but the future value of Guangdong Hao coupons will depend on the adequacy of its preparations. All parties hope that Chen Jitang will not reduce the reserve fund of Guangdong Hao coupons at this time of handover, so as to avoid falling Guangdong finance into an irretrievable place. Montreux Plenary Session Passes New Convention Draft; Two Protocols to Be Signed Tonight; Turkey to Restore Fortifications in the Straits Immediately; Two Japanese Training Ships Permitted to Enter and Exit the Black Sea Simultaneously

Montreux The Montreux Conference held a plenary session this afternoon and immediately passed the draft of the new Straits Convention. It was decided that the initial signing would take place at 10:00 PM on Monday (July 20th). In addition, the conference also passed two protocols. The first allows Turkey to re-establish fortifications in the Dardanelles and Bosphorus Straits from the 20th of this month. The various articles of the new convention will be provisionally implemented by Turkey from August 15th. The second allows two Japanese training ships to pass through the straits simultaneously. The original text is as follows: "Of the three Japanese naval training ships reaching the end of their service life, it has been agreed that two of them may pass through the straits into the Black Sea simultaneously, and their total tonnage, even if it exceeds 15,000 tons, will be treated as such." (Note: The tonnage of warships from any non-Black Sea littoral state allowed to pass through the straits is limited to 15,000 tons.) (18th Havas Dispatch)

Montreux Yesterday afternoon, the Montreux Conference held an open meeting and passed the final draft of the Straits Convention, which includes a protocol stating that Turkey can provisionally implement the conditions of the convention from August 15th. Turkey has the right to immediately re-establish military defenses in the straits. The protocol takes effect from the date of signing the convention. The Turkish government is scheduled to host a banquet next Monday evening to entertain the delegations of the participating countries. A public meeting will be held at 10:00 PM that night to sign the convention. It is reported that Turkish representatives are preparing to send urgent telegrams to Ankara and Istanbul after the signing, whereupon troops from both locations will depart to enter the demilitarized zone. Before the final draft of the convention was passed yesterday afternoon, representatives gave speeches. The Greek representative, Poletis, stated that it was the first act of restoring international law, and that Turkey could now be seen as the standard-bearer for this action. The Turkish representative, Karalas, announced that the Turkish government was determined to maintain the provisions of the Treaty of Lausanne regarding the preservation of cemeteries in the straits and war zones and to allow people to visit them. The British representative, Stanley, rose to express his gratitude for Turkey's commitment. The Australian representative, Bruce, said that Australia would warmly welcome this. The French representative, Peng Gu, also expressed France's gratitude. The Japanese representative, Sato, said that this was the first international agreement signed by Japan since its unfortunate departure from the League of Nations. The audience paid attention to this. According to the provisions of the convention, the Dardanelles Strait is prohibited to warships of belligerent countries during Turkey's neutrality, except for those fulfilling obligations under the League of Nations. Aircraft are also not allowed to fly over the fortified area. Italy did not have a representative present at this meeting, but is able to sign the agreement at any time. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

Montreux The Montreux Conference convened today to discuss the draft of the new convention. The Bulgarian representative immediately stated that he would no longer reserve his position on the Japanese amendment (the content of which advocates that the measures Turkey may take in accordance with the League of Nations Covenant should be implemented only after the League of Nations Council, by a two-thirds majority, and a majority of the signatory countries of the new convention have approved them; this has been satisfied in principle by the Montreux Conference). The Romanian representative also said that his country originally argued that the measures Turkey could take in the event of a danger of war should only be decided by the League of Nations, but now he no longer opposes the Japanese amendment. Thereupon, Sato (Ambassador to France), the chief Japanese representative, thanked Romania, but said that Japan still always reserves a free attitude towards the League of Nations Covenant and the various regional conventions concluded within the scope of the Covenant. The Soviet representative then spoke, saying that Japan had the right to make this reservation, but the Soviet Union fundamentally disagreed with Japan's opinion. Sato then declared that although the Japanese delegation had accepted the draft of the new convention, it would not take effect until it had been approved by the Privy Council of his country, which was a necessary procedure according to the constitution of his country. Thereupon, the meeting immediately opened to the public and announced that a compromise had been reached on the draft of the new convention. Peng Gu (former Minister without Portfolio), the chief French representative, declared that it was an innovation for an international conference to achieve such results. The reason was that Turkey had requested amendments to the treaty through legal procedures. Other representatives also expressed their admiration for the attitude taken by Turkey. The meeting then adjourned.

Turkish Capital Following the conclusion of the Montreux Convention, well-informed sources here recently stated that the Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Agreement previously concluded between Britain and Turkey has now expired due to the cancellation of sanctions against Italy. However, Turkey should still fulfill the unilateral obligations it bears to Britain under this agreement. (19th Havas Dispatch)

(London) It is widely rumored here today that the German government will reply imminently to the British government's questions regarding Hitler's peace plan for Western Europe. It is reported that its reply will be more satisfactory to Britain than expected. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

Seeking International Cooperation Based on the Concept of Equality; British Foreign Secretary Reaffirms Policy

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden recently delivered a speech in Bradford, reiterating that the British government is determined to work with all countries on an equal footing in order to ease international tensions. He said, "If we want to achieve the goal of easing international tensions, we cannot achieve anything by acting alone. Since the March 7th incident (namely, Germany's abandonment of the Locarno Treaty and the entry of troops into the Rhineland), every stage of British policy can be explained by this idea. What we seek is to seek new opportunities for cooperation among European countries in this incident, in order to find ways to solve the general situation in Europe. Our attitude towards previous international conferences is based on this determination, and we should continue to do our best to work hard together whenever we have the opportunity to make lasting progress in the European situation. However, if anyone, because of our country's love of peace, wants to tempt our country to abandon its vital interests as the price of peace, then it can be said that he misunderstands the British character very much. We have repeatedly stated that we have special interests in certain parts of Europe, and therefore we have the obligation to maintain certain guarantees in those parts. This attitude has never changed, but it is not correct to conclude from this that Britain is indifferent to other parts of Europe, because Europe is geographically very small, and we cannot separate areas that should be concerned from those that should not." (18th Havas Dispatch)

British House of Commons; Heavy Workload This Week; Debate on National Defense Procedures Today

(London) The work of the House of Commons will be very heavy next week. On Monday, it will debate the government's national defense procedures. The first speaker will be Sir Inskip, Minister for the Coordination of Defense. On Tuesday, Wednesday, and Thursday, it will consider the motion to approve the new relief unemployment draft issued on July 8th. (18th Reuters Dispatch)

Locarno Conference of Allied Nations to Open; Britain Drafts Declaration; France Will Not Allow Britain to Over-Compromise with Germany

(London) The French Ambassador to London, Gorping, informed Foreign Secretary Eden today that France had agreed to Eden's proposal to hold the future conference of the three Locarno Treaty signatory countries, Britain, France, and Belgium, in London instead of Beijing. The conference will probably open next week on the 23rd and will last for a very short time, as it will be limited to registering the resolutions already obtained through diplomatic channels. (18th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Regarding the issue of a joint declaration issued by Britain, France, and Belgium before and after the opening of the Locarno Conference, it is reported by well-informed sources here that difficulties have arisen, because the British government is currently drafting two versions of the declaration, one declaring the agenda of the three-country conference, and the other declaring that the purpose of the future five-country conference is to revise the Locarno Treaty and formulate new methods for solving Europe based on the principle of equality among countries and taking into account the peace plan announced by German leader Hitler on March 31. However, the French government does not agree with the content of the second declaration, believing that the peace plan proposed by France on April 8 should also be taken into account, and that it should not only be able to accommodate the German plan. The French government also believes that if the resolutions that the three-country conference can reach are negotiated before the meeting, then the meeting will no longer have any meaning. It is reported that the first declaration can be drafted immediately, while the second declaration will begin to be drafted after the three-country conference. (18th Havas Dispatch)

Danzig Curbs Opposition Parties; Takes Strict Measures; National Socialist Government Completely Seizes Power; Whether There Will Be Further Developments Remains to Be Seen

(Berlin) Today, the Danzig government put forward strict plans to curb opposition parties, including (1) the government has the right to dissolve groups that spread rumors that seem to endanger the country, (2) the maximum period of detention is extended from three weeks to three months, (3) police orders of a political nature shall not be reviewed by the courts, and (4) politicians are prohibited from serving concurrently as journalists, and contains other provisions. It is said that this order aims to maintain public safety and order in Danzig. (18th Reuters Dispatch) Danzig The Senate today passed a number of radical measures and has completely handed over the power of the Free City to the National Socialist government. According to the new law, all political organizations can be dissolved at any time without notice. The "protective custody" of the people by the government, which originally could not exceed three weeks at most, has now been changed to three months. (18th National Dispatch)

(Paris) Today, a French official stated that suspending Danzig's political guarantees may seem to be an internal decision at first glance, but whether there will be further developments will be watched carefully. At that time, it will be necessary to consider its external repercussions. This is not an issue between France and Germany, but an international event related to the League of Nations. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

Warsaw After the Danzig authorities took amazing measures today to revoke the various freedoms stipulated in the constitution, responsible persons here recently stated that these measures were purely intended to deal with internal affairs, and that the international impact they could have was within the purview of the League of Nations and was not something that Poland was willing to intervene in alone. What Poland is paying attention to is only to protect its own interests, and there are no other ambitions. Political figures also stated that the Polish government had anticipated the events that had recently occurred in the city. However, the Polish government has always remained neutral in the city's party disputes. Now that the city authorities have taken new measures, the Polish government will naturally study them, but should be based purely on Polish interests. Government officials believe that the dispute between Poland and Danzig has ended since the German National Socialist Party came to power. Now that the Socialist Party, the Catholic Central Party, and the National Right Party have formed a faction, it is not what the Polish government wants to hear if they regain power. On the opposition side, it is believed that the measures taken by Danzig will inevitably endanger Polish interests, but the government is taking a passive attitude, which is very reprehensible, and it is said that Colonel Beck, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, has recently been staying on the Polish coast, which is not far from Danzig. He met with Ambassador to Germany Lipski and was introduced by Babey, the Polish High Commissioner to Danzig, to contact the city authorities. Then, Chairman Glazer of the city council, regarding the guarantees provided by Babey, that the actions taken by the city council to suppress the opposition parties would never go beyond the scope of the free city's system, Beck must have known it. Today, most of the people in the city harbor pro-Polish tendencies and are willing to belong to Poland's protection. This is a phenomenon that has not occurred for hundreds of years. The government should make every effort to protect Poland's rights in Danzig at this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity, and never give up lightly. (18th Havas Dispatch)

(London) After the Danzig authorities took amazing measures to revoke the various freedoms stipulated in the constitution, political figures here recently stated that politicians from Britain and France may informally discuss the Danzig issue during the Anglo-French-Belgian conference in London, because the Council of the League of Nations decided at its meeting earlier this month to entrust Britain, France, and Portugal to jointly investigate the Danzig issue with Poland. In addition, Britain and France may suggest convening a meeting of the Council of the League of Nations to deal with this matter, but no decision will be made until Lester, the League of Nations High Commissioner to Danzig, submits a report. Travelogue of Japan

— (5) Our Reporter Hu Zhongchi, Hu Yizang

(4) Kobe City Hall

The next morning, we went to the Consulate General again and met with Consul General Jiang Huaben. Consul General Jiang has a long history in the diplomatic field, having served as a chargé d'affaires and stationed in Kobe for several years. His smiling, mature, and round face made us feel close at first sight. We discussed the itinerary of the trip with him and planned to stay in Kobe for another day to visit the City Hall and several newspapers. Consul General Jiang prepared several letters of introduction for us. We took the letters, got into a "Taxi" outside the consulate, and went straight to the City Hall.

The Kobe City Hall is located in Tachibana Street, Minato East Ward, and is a magnificent building in the shape of a mouth. The facade is a three-story building, and the other three rows are two-story buildings, with a large courtyard in the middle planted with several banana trees. In front of the door is a raised, large square built of cement. Our car drove up from the road along a gentle slope to the door. Looking up, we could see two intersecting arcs made of cement on the high lintel, which, like a sign on Mount Suwa, is the coat of arms of Kobe. As soon as we entered the gate, we saw a messenger in a police uniform sitting at a small table inside the door on the right. We handed him our business cards and asked to see Mayor Katsuta Ginjiro. He led us upstairs and waited for a moment in the Mayor's reception room. Then Secretary Kai Gunki came out and talked to us on behalf of Mayor Guang. We asked about the recent development of Kobe, and he answered us one by one as follows:

I heard that Kobe's foreign trade has seen great development in recent years. I wonder how it compares to other commercial ports in your country?

Kobe Port's foreign trade used to be inferior to Yokohama in terms of exports and superior to Yokohama in terms of imports, but in recent years both exports and imports have exceeded Yokohama. Last year, the total amount of foreign trade in this port was about 13 million yuan, accounting for one-third of the total national trade. Among the three major trading ports in Japan, Kobe ranks first in terms of the total amount of import and export trade, Yokohama ranks second, and Osaka ranks third.

We have always admired the encouragement and protection that the administrative authorities of your major cities give to industry and commerce. Please tell me what methods your city has adopted in this regard.

Our city's Minato River Park has a Promotion Hall. If the industrial and commercial sectors want to hold a commodity sample display, exhibition, or Bo Jue meeting, they can borrow that place as a venue. The government will naturally do its best to provide guidance. In addition, we are constantly planning and implementing appropriate methods for rewarding and introducing local industry and commerce. The Industry and Commerce Section of our city hall has a specialist stationed in Manchuria to handle the introduction of our city's industry and commerce. In addition, the city hall is also investigating the status of industry and commerce in our city and publishes "Kobe City Commercial and Industrial Overview" and "Kobe City Commercial and Industrial Directory" every year for general industrial and commercial operators to refer to.

Your office must also be very concerned about the welfare of the working-class citizens. I wonder if there are any special facilities to give them practical benefits in life?

The social undertakings carried out by this city are similar to those in other cities in this country. There is nothing special to say. In addition to running many agencies related to public health, we also have many public canteens and common lodgings for the poor laborers, thinking about their food and lodging. The nature of the public canteen is to provide clean and nutritious food to workers at very low cost. There are five types of meal tickets, the lowest is a three-cent ticket, and the highest is an eleven-cent set meal ticket. The common lodging is well-equipped, and each night only costs seventeen cents for accommodation.

Next, we asked Secretary Kai; "How is your city's recent financial situation? What is the average tax burden per citizen?"

He thought for a while, then led us to the Finance Section. It was a very large room. Closely packed old writing desks were filled with Western-suited section members, burying their heads in the cluttered piles of paper. He talked to a section member for a while, turned around and said to us: "The Director of the Finance Section is not here. I can only know about the financial situation in the past year after asking him. However, if you want to know about the Showa 9th year, I can get some printed materials." Kobe City Hall

Page 8

Revolution Breaks Out in Morocco; Chaos Spreads in Spain; Meaning of Cabinet Reshuffle Unclear; Government Claims It Can Control the Overall Situation

Madrid A rebellion broke out in Morocco on Friday, and Prime Minister Quiroga suddenly resigned amid national shock. However, Barrio was immediately appointed as his successor. Barrio came from a typesetting worker background, once served as Prime Minister, and was also the interim President temporarily after President Azana was removed from office in April of this year before President Achina was elected. The significance of Barrio's succession to the cabinet this time is not yet clear. (19th National Dispatch)

Madrid The Quiroga cabinet submitted its general resignation yesterday evening. At that time, the residents of the city of Melilla in Morocco were clashing with the rebels and were being supported by bombers sent by the government. As soon as President Achana received the cabinet's resignation, he immediately appointed Barrio, the Speaker of the House of Representatives, to form a new cabinet, which has now been formed. The list of personnel is as follows:

Prime Minister Barrio (leader of the Unified Republican Party), Foreign Minister Asgarate (former Deputy Secretary-General of the League of Nations), Interior Minister Basia (former Foreign Minister, Left-wing Republican Party), Army Minister General Miazhas (former Acting Army Minister in the Azana cabinet), Navy Minister Chirol (still in office, Left-wing Republican Party), Finance Minister Laemis (still in office, Left-wing Republican Party), Labor Minister Traslivos (former Minister of Communications, Unified Republican Party), Justice Minister Karlson (still in office, Left-wing Republican Party), Communications Minister Lusi (former Minister of Labor, Left-wing Catalan Autonomous Party), Agriculture Minister Ramon Fed (newly appointed, party affiliation unknown), Commerce Minister Puila (still in office, Unified Republican Party), Education Minister Taomingo (former Education Minister in the Azana cabinet), Minister Without Portfolio Roman (newly appointed, leader of the Republican National Party). (19th Havas Dispatch)

Government Fully Suppressing the Rebellion

Madrid - The government issued a broadcast message at noon today, stating that government troops had engaged in street fighting with rebel forces in the port of Barcelona, capturing numerous high-ranking and low-ranking rebel officers and seizing five cannons. At 12:30 PM, another broadcast message announced that the disturbances in Barcelona, Seville, and Malaga had been quelled. The people in all areas are urged to remain calm and composed but to maintain vigilance at all times. The government has sufficient power to deal with all emergencies. At 12:45 PM, another broadcast message stated that the capital is currently very peaceful and that rumors of rebel troops occupying the capital are completely unfounded. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

(Paris) Regarding the situation in Spain, a telegram from semi-official sources in the capital stated that the government has been able to control the overall situation, that four rebel generals have been arrested, and that the plane used by the rebel leader has been intercepted by the government. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

(London) The revolutionary movement initiated by the Spanish Moroccan Legion yesterday has now spread throughout the country with great speed. It is reported that the cities of Melilla and Ceuta in Spanish Morocco have been occupied by the Foreign Legion. A cavalry regiment has been ordered to Seville to suppress the unrest. Troops stationed in Burgos and Pamplona are also said to have rebelled. Disturbances have also occurred on the small islands of the Canary and Balearic Islands. Government aircraft have bombed Melilla and Ceuta. Former Spanish Prime Minister Lerroux has fled to Portugal. British naval and army personnel stationed in Gibraltar have been ordered to refrain from entering Spanish territory from today onwards. The above is the true picture of the current situation in Spain as reported by various sources. However, news coming out of Spain is being heavily censored, making it difficult to ascertain the actual situation. A message from Gibraltar states that according to a Spanish radio station announcement, the government is confident in handling the situation, but a message from a radio station fallen into the hands of the rebels claims that the revolutionaries have won a major victory throughout the country. This afternoon, the government issued a public announcement acknowledging that the disturbances are not limited to Morocco alone and stating that the government has completely recovered certain areas illegally declared under a state of alert by the rebel elements, as well as the small islands of the Balearic and Canary Islands. A message from Madrid this evening acknowledges that Melilla and Ceuta are still occupied by the Foreign Legion, but the authorities express confidence that the disturbances can be completely quelled within 48 hours. According to a report from Madrid, all cities occupied by the rebels have declared a general strike, which proves that the previous reports of unrest on the Balearic and Canary Islands were not rumors. The message also states that two generals were arrested on the Canary Islands. A telegram from Oran reports that news from the Algerian-Moroccan border indicates that government troops and rebel soldiers engaged in fierce fighting, resulting in the deaths of two generals and the capture of more than thirty officers. According to a report from Gibraltar, serious fighting broke out last night between fascists and communists in the city of La Línea near the border, resulting in one death and at least twenty serious injuries. Over a hundred British residents were on their way to the market in La Línea at the time and immediately returned to Gibraltar upon seeing the situation. According to a report from Lisbon, the capital of Portugal, Lerroux, who was responsible for arresting President Azaña last year, has fled from the Spanish border to Portugal. Madrid now announces that the number of dead and wounded in the current disturbances has been very small to date. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Air Force Bombing

Madrid - Although the Spanish government claims that the center of the serious unrest in Morocco is limited to Seville, Burgos, and Pamplona, there are also various reports coming out stating it will soon spread throughout the country. Government secret agents are currently engaged in searching for the leaders of various fascist and leftist factions throughout the country, as they are suspected of plotting a counter-revolution. This morning, the authorities here issued an official radio message stating that a cavalry regiment has been dispatched to Seville. All workers in areas declared under a state of alert by the anti-government forces have been urged by union leader Caballero, via radio broadcast, to declare... There are indeed several places in Spain with unrest, but they express confidence that this movement will be limited in nature and will not expand. According to government sources, the disturbances in Morocco have been suppressed after several fierce battles between troops loyal to the government and rebel soldiers. Army aircraft have played a major role in this battle. The disturbances broke out yesterday in Melilla and Ceuta in northwestern Spanish Morocco. Twenty thousand soldiers of the Foreign Legion stationed there mutinied. It is said that nine people were killed when residents of Melilla declared a general strike in an attempt to resist the mutineers. Three people were also killed when the disturbance occurred in the local area. The Commissioner's Office has been occupied by the mutineers. After news of the outbreak of the above disturbances reached Madrid, two flagships of the Spanish Navy were immediately dispatched from Cartagena to Morocco, while all troops loyal to the government were also ordered to suppress the unrest. Last night, news was received here that army aircraft were bombing the rebel masses in Melilla and Ceuta. Before long, it was officially confirmed that a strict plan of containment was being adopted to curb the revolutionary movement. A document was published this morning, stating that one foreign aircraft was seized in connection with the disturbances in Morocco. It is said that it was carrying a rebel leader from Morocco to Spain. Yesterday afternoon, the government announced that the rebels had occupied the Ceuta radio station and issued a radio broadcast announcing that disturbances had occurred in Seville, Madrid, and other places. However, according to this morning's bulletin, the whole of Spain is quiet as usual. The rebel party's claim that the Minister of the Army and the Minister of the Interior were captured is completely fabricated. Fortunately, the government has taken swift action to deal with the disturbances, which can now be regarded as extinguished. It is reported that a famous right-wing leader has been murdered by the rebel masses, but this has not yet been confirmed. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Madrid - Last night and this morning, the government officially acknowledged via radio that the rebellion in Morocco has spread to mainland Spain. Initially, it was only claimed that the troops in Seville had rebelled, but it was later acknowledged that it had spread to Malaga and Cádiz. A spokesman for the Ministry of the Interior stated that the momentum of the rebels is gradually weakening. It is reported that forty armed workers forcibly boarded a ship docked in the port of Barcelona, seized fifty rifles, and were then suppressed by the mobile guard team, who recovered the seized firearms. The government ordered the dissolution of the rebel army last night and dismissed the governor of the Canary Islands. At the same time, it used warships to transport an army unit to carry out the duties of the government. Minister of the Interior Moles announced on the radio last night that government aircraft had begun to bomb key rebel locations in Morocco. As for Spain itself, the Minister of the Interior stated that all troops are loyal to the government, so the government has ample power to deal with the incidents in Morocco, and the public should not pay attention to them. The government, in view of the urgency of the situation, has taken decisive measures to arrest several military officers. It is understood that several officers in the navy have also been dismissed for disobeying orders. Airmail throughout Spain has been completely suspended since yesterday, but mail planes from other countries can still land, but only with prior permission. The Minister of the Interior also said that the government had seized a foreign aircraft and would use it to fly to Morocco to bring back a certain rebel leader. (National Telegram, 19th)

Rebel Forces Have Great Momentum

Gibraltar - It is rumored that the Spanish Moroccan rebel army, which landed in Cádiz today, is now advancing towards Seville, intending to join forces with the rebels there in order to advance on the capital, Madrid. (Reuters dispatch, 19th)

Tangier, North Africa - According to a broadcast message from Seville, General Del Llano, Deputy Commander of the Seville garrison, has joined the rebel army, calling himself the "Liberation Army" and issuing a proclamation calling on the people to support him. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Radio Propaganda War

Madrid - Since the mutiny of the garrison in the Spanish Moroccan territory of North Africa, the "United Radio Station" here and the radio station in Ceuta, North Africa, have been issuing reports via radio broadcasts. The former acts as the government's mouthpiece, while the latter has been occupied by the rebel army, and their propaganda is diametrically opposed, with each side engaging in a war of words, as if waging a radio war. For example, the Ceuta radio station issued a message stating that the warships dispatched by the government to patrol the Moroccan coast had fallen into the hands of the rebel army and were now returning to the Spanish coast. The "United Radio Station" immediately issued a broadcast bulletin at 5:15 PM today, denying this claim, stating that the warships were always loyal to the government and were now ordered to proceed to the African coast and would arrive soon. It also said that only a small part of the Moroccan garrison had defected, that the local civil administration was still loyal to the government, that all people should obey the orders of the civil officials, and that no martial law had been declared in Morocco, etc. This bulletin also published a telegram from right-wing member of parliament Lucia expressing loyalty to the government. (Note: Lucia is a member of the Autonomist Party of the Province of France and is affiliated with the Spanish right-wing parties united under the leadership of former Minister of the Army Robles, who is not tolerated by the current government and has already fled to France.) At 7:45 PM, the "United Radio Station" issued another broadcast bulletin, stating that all provinces across the country were now loyal to the government, that the disturbances that had occurred in some cities had been quickly quelled, and that although rebel General Queipo had illegally declared martial law in Seville, his rebel troops had surrendered to government troops, and that a cavalry regiment had entered the city to the cheers of the people, who shouted "Long live the Spanish Republic" to show their welcome. It also stated that the government was now able to completely control the situation. In addition, the socialist trade unions in the capital have decided to automatically hold a general strike in places where martial law has been declared, and will not resume work until order has been restored. This decision has been announced by the leader of the extreme wing of the Socialist Party, Caballero, in the name of various associations and labor organizations, and broadcast by the "United Radio Station" to various locations. (Havas dispatch, 18th)

Key Figures Behind the Coup

(Paris) A reporter for the Petit Parisien, reporting from Perpignan (near the Spanish border in southern France), stated: "The coup in Spain was initiated by three people: the leader of the right-wing Catholic Party, Robles, General Sanjurjo (who was arrested and sentenced to death in August 1932 for causing unrest, but the sentence was later commuted to life imprisonment, and he was only pardoned in April 1934), and the son of former dictator Rivera, who is currently in prison but has prison guards colluding with him. Their planned scheme was to have Sotelo (leader of the monarchist party, recently assassinated) as the leader of the new government. The security forces have agreed to support this, because the security forces are mostly right-wing and have had long-standing conflicts with the left-wing stormtroopers, and thus participated in the coup." (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Perpignan, France - The Associated Press recently learned from reliable sources that the mutiny of the garrison in Melilla, Morocco, was actually a nationwide revolutionary plan, which unfortunately erupted prematurely before it was fully developed. According to this plan, it was formed in the home of peasant party leader Robles last month. Among those who participated in the conspiracy were Rivera, the son of the late Spanish dictator, and three army generals and militia officers. Rivera was still in prison for privately storing weapons at the time, but was released by prison guards. The original plan was for the garrisons in Morocco and the Canary Islands to mutiny at the same time, and after succeeding, they would return to their country. At that time, the domestic army would also respond, and a new government would be formed with Conservative Party leader Sotelo as president. However, Sotelo was suddenly assassinated in Madrid on July 13, which led to the premature launch of the Melilla army before the timing was ripe. (National Telegram, 18th)

(Paris) The Figaro reporter stationed in Madrid, after arriving at the French border, spoke with the newspaper by long-distance telephone. According to him, the plan for the coup in Spain was jointly drafted by the monarchists and the fascists. Its contents are roughly as follows: (1) Start the uprising in the territory of Morocco in North Africa. The officers there are mostly members of the monarchist party. Even the foreign legion and Moorish native soldiers can come out and respond. (2) After Morocco launches the uprising, the government must mobilize a large army to suppress the country's south. Once this unit arrives, it must follow up with a mutiny. (3) Within the mainland, simultaneous uprisings should be held in the west, east, and southeast, and an attack on the city of Madrid should be launched. (A) In the west, a general should sneak into Galicia from Portugal and launch an uprising. (B) In the east, in the province of Pamplona, another general should lead the garrison to resist the government. (C) The garrison in the southeast should also rise up in response. In addition, the rebel side believes that although the government has cut off all telegraphs and telephones, the rebels can mobilize the air force personnel at the Burgos air force base to participate in the rebellion and relay information. (Havas dispatch, 19th)

Where is the Hirota Cabinet Going? (3)

- Jia He

Hirota seemed not satisfied with the above denials, and was filled with the ambition, singing a duet with Seiyukai's famous liberalist Uehara Etsujiro in the budget meeting. Uehara first affirmatively said, "Those who receive the great command, if they cannot freely choose their cabinet members, then the perfect operation of constitutional politics cannot be expected." Then he talked about Hirota's cabinet formation process, questioning, "What was the Prime Minister's experience in this cabinet formation?"

Hirota replied, "It is possible for those who receive the great command to have someone deemed suitable recommended by the army internally."

"That's probably wrong! According to the practice up to today, the selection of the Minister of the Army is decided and recommended among the three chiefs, that's a well-known fact."

"What I said is not wrong."

Uehara then questioned, "The world generally believes that there is a military department outside the government... what is the Prime Minister's view?" Hirota resolutely answered him, "I have heard people say that, and I intend to work hard to ensure that such a thing does not happen." This kind of strong argument that completely obliterates the facts is to show the military department that today's Hirota is not the Hirota of the past. Therefore, when Mimuroto Keikozi re-submitted the question of the state of mind of cabinet formation on May 12, he told the House of Peers about the situation of Kusunoki's sword breaking and arrows running out at Minatogawa. We know that when Kusunoki Masashige devoted his loyalty to the Japanese imperial family, there was already a struggle between the Northern and Southern Dynasties. We do not yet know the detailed inside story of the "February 26th" coup, but isn't it strange that Hirota Kōki dares to claim to be Kusunoki Masashige? Please chew on this carefully, every expert.

The Hirota Cabinet not only denied its raped-like ambition when forming the cabinet in front of the parliament, but also joined hands with political parties to question the military department and criticize the military department. The most brilliant was the speech by Saito Takao of the Minseito Party. This speech with a historical mission was published by the newspapers of Japanese property owners in extremely large coverage. Except for Murobuse Takashin's sarcastic "Its sound is sad" (read the evening edition of May 12), the Osaka Mainichi praised it as "the voice of the people" (May 9). The Toa Asahi called it "Every sentence is the word of the people." An unprecedented emotion was reflected in the parliament, and regardless of faction, they responded with warm applause. Ando Masazumi (Seiyukai), who originally planned to deliver the same speech, also automatically withdrew.

Saito Takao used beautiful words to point out the following points: "First is the interference of the military in politics." He said, "It is an indisputable fact that active-duty soldiers talk about politics and participate in political activities. What attitude will the military department take towards this?" He first quoted the Meiji Emperor's decree to the military and Ito Hirobumi's constitutional interpretation to prove that soldiers cannot interfere in politics. Then, righteously, he put the big hat of violating the imperial decree on the head of the military, and also pointed out that soldiers have simple thoughts and cannot cope with complex social situations, are easily used by others, and even resort to direct action. "May 15th" is a living proof. After this conclusion, he turned around and asked General Terauchi, "What is the Minister of the Army's opinion on this point?" Second, he criticized the military department's attitude towards handling every major incident. He quoted the famous author of Nihon Gaishi, Rai Sanyo, criticizing the reason why medieval regimes were handed over to the military: "The successive dynasties" adopted an attitude of appeasement and leniency towards the Minamoto and Taira clans, and did not know the foundation and "the disaster of fighting and seizing" to warn the Minister of the Army, and shouted, "If soldiers form a party and openly break into the Prime Minister's official residence in broad daylight and shoot the Prime Minister of the country appointed by His Majesty the Emperor, seize the weapons given to them for the purpose of protecting the country, and assassinate the highest-ranking minister of the country in charge of political affairs, the seriousness of the crime, "Indeed there is no need to dwell on it." He also painfully revealed how the army destroyed the country's legal dignity and criticized the military department for harming Yamamoto, the prosecutor who advocated bringing the participants in the coup to justice during the "May 15th" incident. Finally, he drew the conclusion of the coup responsibility: "The military department's attitude towards a certain incident sighed out the ×× incident; the military department's attitude towards the ×× incident called out the "May 15th" incident; the military department's attitude towards the "May 15th" incident really caused a major ominous event." Third, he publicly stated that recent young people's behavior, "one is carried out in the name of patriotism, and one is carried out in the name of the proletariat." Both this right-leaning and left-leaning are harmful to the country's great cause of constitutional monarchy, and there is absolutely no way for our people to advance beyond this."; and revealed the mission of the current stage of the Hirota cabinet. Fourth, he seemed to face the Seiyukai parliamentary seat and shouted, "If politicians other than the military department collude with a part of the military department and conspire and want to carry out political ambitions, if there are such people, then they must not be let go. If a constitutional politician takes the people as the background, they should stand upright in front of the masses, plan for the country, and engage in political strife with fair and just means. As for plotting behind the scenes and attempting unstable conspiracies, they must not be allowed by constitutional politicians."

The Rapid Advancement of Soviet Aviation; Air Force Strength Surpasses European and American Powers; Civilian Activities Repeatedly Set Impressive Records

Special Dispatch from the China United Press: The Soviet government's efforts to promote aviation have been tireless, and the results have surpassed those of European and American powers, making it a world-class aviation nation. Recalling the period after the October Revolution, the entire country was in a state of chaos, and all industries were in decline. By 1921, the government, recognizing that the Soviet Union was a vast continental nation, considered the construction of an air force to be a matter of urgency to protect the victory of the revolution and defend against foreign aggression. Therefore, a plan was established and actively implemented. Non-military aviation activities did not begin until 1923, lasting only fourteen years. As a result, it now dominates the world of aviation. Its spirit of striving for progress is truly worthy of emulation. Therefore, the current state of aviation in the country is introduced below, so that those concerned about national defense issues may be alerted.

Air Force Power

In 1922, the Soviet Air Force had only 20 land-based squadrons. By 1925, it had increased to 80 squadrons, and in 1928, it increased to 100 squadrons. Now it has reached more than 350 squadrons, with over 4,000 aircraft. The increase and development of fighter planes and bombers are particularly astonishing. It is estimated that after the success of the Second Five-Year Plan, it will reach as many as 8,000 aircraft. The various materials for expanding the air force were purchased from Germany, Italy, England, and France, and specialists were hired from these countries to be responsible for building aircraft factories. However, after the success of the First Five-Year Plan, due to the active promotion of the development of the aviation industry and its raw material resources, and the large-scale training of technical specialists, it is now able to completely manufacture new and advanced aircraft itself. The most distinctive feature of the Soviet Air Force is the airborne landing force and the troop transport aircraft currently under construction. Moreover, parachute technology is extremely widespread in the country, something that European and American countries cannot match. This airborne landing force is intended to outflank the enemy's rear. The exercise held near the capital of the Ukrainian Republic, Kyiv, last September was very successful, and the people of the world were greatly impacted at the time.

Civil Aviation

The Soviet government's planning and management of civil aviation construction, such as the opening of air routes and the training of aviators, are also centered on national defense, so that they can be quickly converted to military use in case of emergency. According to the authorities, in 1923, the country had only 12 foreign-made aircraft, and the total length of air routes was only 1,666 kilometers. The total number of passengers throughout the year was only 3,000, and the amount of goods transported was 21,291 grams. But by the end of 1935, the number of aircraft had increased to thousands, and the total length of air routes had reached 77,000 kilometers. According to statistics, the total number of passengers last year was 111,000, the amount of mail transported was 6,600 tons, and the amount of goods was 5,000 tons. Comparing these huge numbers with those of twelve years ago reveals the speed of its advancement and development.

Special Contributions

Soviet civilian aircraft are not only used for transportation and traffic, but are also very active in special work and have made great contributions, such as photographic surveying, Arctic exploration, capturing fish and marine animals, eliminating pests, and sowing seeds. Excellent results have been achieved in all of these areas. According to statistics, last year a total of 35 million hectares of forest area were surveyed, 120,000 hectares of fields were sown, 560,000 hectares of agricultural and forestry pests and animals were eliminated, and 2,435,000 hectares of "malaria mosquitoes" were eliminated.

Setting New Records

Under the promotion and encouragement of the government, the Soviet people have a strong interest in aviation and often create impressive new records. Important achievements include staying in the air for 75 hours, flying a long distance of 12,411 kilometers, ascending to an altitude of 11,080 meters, performing a parachute jump of 7,612 meters, and stratospheric flights of 15,000 meters. All of these broke previous world or Soviet records and won warm praise from the global aviation community.

Arctic Flight

In addition to enriching and expanding its domestic aviation industry, the Soviet authorities also devoted all their efforts to the development of Arctic air routes. As a result, Molokov completed the flight from Moscow via Sverdlovsk, Skrobirsk, Kurasloselsk, and Iolkatuvdinka to Jingksheng Island. At the same time, aviators Viatapiyalov and Lin Qili also completed the voyage between Moscow and Simit Bay, a distance of 13,500 kilometers. All of these have written a glorious page in the history of Soviet aviation, providing a strong impetus for backward countries.

Flooding in Hebei Province; Daming City Surrounded by Water; Torrential Floods Make Rescue Impossible; Traffic Cut Off and Food Prices Soar

(Tianjin) The Cangxian city river was backflowing from the rising waters of the Grand Canal, and the water was surging. At 6:00 AM on the 18th, 60 zhang of the new dike at Xingjiazhuang collapsed. The water is flowing in the ocean, and the plains are four or five feet deep. Dozens of villages along the river have been flooded. County Magistrate Yu Zhenqing led the militia to the area on the 19th to gather civilians to reinforce the dike. The water in the Zhang River in southern Hebei is rising again. More than a hundred villages in the old levee area of the first, second, and third districts of Daming County, such as Shuangjing Town, have been submerged. The torrential floods are impossible to rescue. Daming County is now in the center of the water. County Magistrate Ma Runchang, in cooperation with Chen Chunrong's brigade of the 29th Army and Ma Shibin's troops of the Ninth Security District, mobilized the entire force for rescue. The current water level in the city river continues to rise. The Western school yard has been submerged. Soldiers and civilians are defending day and night. The Da-Han-Ping and Da-Liang motorways have been submerged, cutting off external traffic, and food prices are soaring. Residents are panicking. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) The rising water of the South Canal is depositing silt downstream, raising the Hai River by one foot in five days. All dredging vessels have been mobilized to dredge. Giant ships with a draft of more than 14 feet have stopped sailing to Tianjin. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) The Hebei-Chahar Association plans to take over the dredging of the Hai River from the North China Water Conservancy Bureau, and the powers and responsibilities will be assigned to the Construction Committee of the Association. A separate agency will be established to be responsible for this. However, the current management fee is only 120,000 yuan per month. After the takeover, it will increase to 250,000 yuan. The shortfall is being telegraphed to the Economic Commission for approval. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) The South Canal rose four inches again on the night of the 18th and the morning of the 19th. The second section of the dike at Botou Town was washed away and pushed against the main dike, causing continuous dangerous situations. The River Bureau continued to purchase 4,000 hemp bags on the 19th and transported them to Nancun and Wuqing Counties to supervise the civilians in reinforcing the dike. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Flood Control and Risk Prevention Association telegraphed the counties upstream of each river to immediately inform them if there are mountain floods or increased water levels so that they can be prepared. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Jinan) Kong Xiangrong passed through Jinan today on his way to Qingdao. The project to straighten the mouth of the Yellow River and divert the river has been completed, and 40% of the diversion has been completed, and the water flow is smooth. (Special dispatch, 19th)

Smuggled Artificial Silk Made into Bolts of Cloth and Sold as Local Products in the Interior; The Silk Industry is Also Affected

(Nanjing) In the past, unscrupulous merchants and Japanese ruffians smuggled a large number of artificial silk to Zhoucun County and other places along the Jiaoji Railway, made them into bolts of cloth, and sold them as local products in the interior to avoid the attention of the customs. As a result, the sales of the silk industry in Jiangsu and Zhejiang have also been encroached upon recently. It is expected that after the implementation of the inspection and handling measures for the artificial silk purchased by each factory and the bolts of cloth made of artificial silk or mixed with artificial silk and sold as local products, which will be promulgated by the Ministry of Finance this time, the aforementioned disguised smuggling can be stopped. In other news, the Customs Anti-Smuggling General Inspection Office for Road Transportation has established anti-smuggling sub-offices along the Jinpu and Pinghan Railways. However, the Beijing-Shenyang Railway is still lacking, so smuggling on that railway is still rampant, and legitimate commercial interests, both Chinese and foreign, are suffering. The Japanese legitimate merchants in particular have suffered severe losses. It is reported that the government has indeed made arrangements for anti-smuggling measures on the Beijing-Shenyang Railway, which will be implemented within days. It is still undetermined when Ansell will go north. (CNA dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) In order to prevent Japanese ruffians from relying on Fengtai on the Beijing-Shenyang Railway as a center to forcibly transport smuggled goods to the Pinghan and Pingsui Railways, Tianjin Customs is negotiating with the Beijing-Shenyang Railway to establish an inspection sub-office in Yangcun. The railway side agrees that as long as the diplomatic difficulties are overcome, they can assist. This matter will be discussed and decided after Ansell arrives in Tianjin. (Special dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) Because the customs has designated the raw materials for artificial silk woven goods as smuggled goods, the factories weaving these goods have been ordered to pay supplementary taxes before exporting them. Dozens of factories in Tianjin that are engaged in this industry have been shut down. The factory side has again submitted a petition to the Tianjin Customs Supervision Department, stating that there is no place to purchase legitimate artificial silk other than smuggled goods. If the government does not have a fundamental method to suppress smuggled goods, all factories will be forced to shut down. (Special dispatch, 19th)

People in Guangxi Province Fleeing to Guizhou

(Guiyang) Recently, many people from Guangxi Province have fled to Guizhou Province. According to reports, after the changes in Guangxi Province following Li Bai's transfer, the young men in each county were forced to be conscripted. Recently, due to the sharp decline in Guangxi currency and the difficulty in military expenses, a livestock tax was reintroduced. A tax of six yuan was levied on each live ox, regardless of size, and a tax of three yuan was levied on each live pig, regardless of size, with a deadline of three days to pay. Currently, more than 2,000 people from Lingyun, Tian'e, and other counties have fled to Luodian in succession. (CNA dispatch, 19th)

Schools in Hebei Province Oppose the Distribution of Education Funds at 85%

(Tianjin) In order to balance revenue and expenditure, the Hebei Provincial Government is distributing educational funds for the 25th year at 85% of the full amount. The schools in Tianjin are opposed and have sent representatives such as Wei Mingchu and six others to the province to petition. The Education Department is also forwarding the petition. (Special dispatch, 19th)

Drought in Eastern Tianjin; Autumn Harvest Hopeless

(Tianjin) Since the beginning of summer, no rain has fallen in the eastern counties of Tianjin. The crops are withering and dying. If it does not rain again, there is a risk that there will be no autumn harvest. (CNA dispatch, 19th)

Beiyang and Hengyuan Cotton Mills to be Sold Due to Poor Performance

(Tianjin) The Beiyang and Hengyuan cotton mills operated by the Tianjin Chengfu Trust Company have been unable to compete due to poor performance and the continued expansion of Japanese factories. After days of meetings and discussions, the result was a decision to sell or increase Japanese shares. Negotiations have now begun. (CNA dispatch, 19th)

(Tianjin) The Japanese textile industry plans to form a front in North China and further oppress the Chinese spinning industry. Toyo Cotton Mill and Kanebo Cotton Mill are buying up cotton mills operated by Chinese in Shijiazhuang, Botou, Tangshan, and other places in order to achieve their monopoly. (Special dispatch, 19th)

Discussing Increased Train Service between Beiping and Shenyang

(Tianjin) The issue of increasing train service between Beiping and Shenyang once is related to technical cooperation and the schedule of trains. It has been decided that another meeting will be held in Beidaihe on the 28th, with the Oriental Travel Agency as the center. Representatives from both the Beijing-Shenyang and Fengshan Railway Bureaus will participate. (Special dispatch, 19th)

Intense Heat in Shaanxi; 108 Degrees

(Xi'an) The heat in Xi'an on the 18th was intense, reaching 108 degrees. The chairs and tables indoors were like hot irons, and there were few pedestrians on the streets. It was one of the hottest days since entering the hottest period of summer. (CNA dispatch, 18th)

Shaanxi Provincial Government Cables Yan to Accept Refugees from Shanxi to Northern Shaanxi

(Xi'an) In the third and fourth months of this year, when the Red bandits fled from Shanxi to northern Shaanxi, they coerced many good people from southern Shanxi. Now that the remnants of the bandits are fleeing west, many people from Shanxi are wandering in northern Shaanxi. The local authorities have made appropriate arrangements for their resettlement. A telegram has been sent to Yan Xishan requesting him to send personnel to northern Shaanxi to receive them and send them back to their hometowns to ensure their livelihood. (CNA dispatch, 18th)

(Xi'an) With the remnant bandits in northern Shaanxi cleared, the area has become desolate, refugees are displaced, and cultivation has almost ceased. The countryside needs to be restored urgently. The military and political authorities have decided to allocate 300,000 yuan from the Farmers Bank to handle farmers' loans, with Suide and Yongchuan as the center. Loan personnel from Suide set off on the 18th, and the loan regulations have also been announced. (CNA dispatch, 18th)

The main force of the Ma Division flanked the bandits at Lizhabao and Hanfuwan via Haiyuan Zhengqibao. (2) The bandits near Anbian were fiercely attacked by our army on the 11th and 12th, and the bandits suffered heavy casualties. (3) According to a telegram from County Magistrate Jia of Haiyuan on the 11th, due to the continuous attacks by our army in recent days, the bandits are unable to withstand it. There are no traces of bandits in Wangjiatuan Village and Tongxin. The bandits in Heicheng Town have all fled. However, there are still remnants of bandits temporarily holding out in Liwangbao Qiyingchuan and other places, but it will be difficult for them to stay there for long. (CNA dispatch, 18th)
