Anecdotes of the Southern Tour

— Special Correspondent Shi Ying

The Unfortunate Women of Eastern Zhejiang

Starting from Lanxi's West Gate, walking along the riverside to the South Gate, and looking southwest across the river, there's a shuttle-shaped green mountain called Hengshan. It's a crucial convergence point for the Changshan, Quzhou, Gangtou, and Wu Gang rivers. At the mountain's eastern foot and halfway up, there are temples. Emperor Wuzong of the Ming Dynasty inscribed the four characters "Lanyin Shenchu" (Deep Seclusion of Lanxi) on the mountainside's stone wall. Bringing your gaze back, you see the green mountain and white temple reflected in the river. With the occasional sails, it truly resembles a beautiful painting of misty light and cloud shadows. If you bring your gaze even closer, you'll surely notice many painted boats leaning against the shore and countless small teahouses hanging low along the riverbank. These are the pleasure grounds where wealthy merchants indulge in sensual desires, and also the sinful places where unfortunate women are forced to sell their bodies.

It's unknown when flower boats first appeared in Lanxi. However, according to records, they started during the Hong Yang period (Taiping Rebellion). This place is a major land and water transportation hub in eastern Zhejiang, and its commerce is increasingly prosperous. Around 1919 and 1920, there were as many as ninety flower boats, which could be considered the peak of the industry. Later, in 1927, due to the impact of military affairs, the boats were moved to pontoon bridges, and the flower boats suffered as collateral damage. Furthermore, with the construction of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, the number of tourists sharply decreased, and the flower boat business declined dramatically. Last autumn, there were still twenty-seven boats, but now that number has decreased to twenty. Each flower boat has five or six young women, commonly called "boat girls" or "female boat owners" (meaning "female signboard"). Tourists can sit on the boat for a while and be offered tea and cigarettes without spending money. However, if they eat a banquet, request songs, or play mahjong, they often spend lavishly. But in reality, it ultimately has a great negative impact on good morals. The county government once planned to strictly ban them, but feared that the boat owners and boat girls would be unable to make a living, so they could only adopt a gradual policy, hoping to remedy the situation slowly. Currently, all the boat girls on each boat are bought by the boat owners as "adopted daughters" from poor and remote villages at a young age. On the surface, their lives seem to be spent in romantic and carefree pursuits, but the suffering they actually endure is a living hell on earth. In addition, upstream counties also have flower boats, which are similarly affected by the decline in commerce, further deepening their tragic fate of inhumane living.

The row of teahouses along the river in Lanxi is built on the riverbank, with the buildings seven or eight steps lower than the street. If you go to drink tea, it's more accurate to say you're going downstairs rather than upstairs. As soon as tourists enter a teahouse and recline on a chair, the local tea girls (about four or five of them) swarm around you, pouring tea and shelling melon seeds, trying to seduce customers in any way they can. If there's more than one tea guest, they seem especially busy, rushing back and forth like a revolving lantern. If the guest wants a cigarette, they magically light the match and quickly light the cigarette you're holding in your mouth. Even more artistically, they perfectly cover the bottom of the plate with a layer of melon seeds, no more, no less. Before you finish the first two plates, the next two are brought out simultaneously. You can only eat so much, but they, as a group, don't hesitate to eat and hide the seeds. In no time, the empty plates are stacked into two pagodas, showing that the income from melon seeds alone is considerable, not to mention the extra tips. According to a gentleman from the county's chamber of commerce, there are about two hundred such teahouses. The leisure and pleasure of the tourists who come to drink tea lies not in the tea itself, but in another realm. The tea girls are also poor women from the countryside, hired by the teahouses with a monthly salary of only three or four yuan. Their hopes for extra income are very low, so many young men who indulge in pleasure fall into the vast river outside the teahouse and can't extricate themselves. The county government has now taken measures to improve the situation, prohibiting them from picking up or seeing off guests outside the teahouse. The reason for this "prohibition" is that there's more to it than just picking up and seeing off guests. Teahouses in neighboring counties, such as Jinhua, Longyou, and Jiangshan, have also suffered from this spreading disease. Recently, an assassination case occurred in Qu County, which was found to be related to teahouse waitresses. Due to the strict ban by the local garrison, the flowers of the teahouses, like lost dogs, have had to flee to neighboring counties. Lanxi, as their birthplace, is especially hoped for, but even with strong defenses, it's impossible to resist.

Lanxi and Jinhua counties still have the bad custom of "valuing men over women," which is also a factor in creating "boat girls," "tea girls," and "local prostitutes." Generally, middle-class families are unwilling to raise too many girls, and poor farmers are even more unwilling to raise girls. Therefore, when a girl is born, they are sometimes treated with barbaric methods (the county government has already issued a notice prohibiting this), or secretly abandoned in front of wealthy families' doors, or the infant is left to the orphanage after sending a letter to inform them. In recent years, as more nannies have been hired in Shanghai and other ports, there have been more abandoned children here.

In particular, the customs in various villages are not open, and marriage is mainly based on money. It's commonly said that it's harder for poor families to marry a wife than to buy farmland. For the sake of future planning, parents are happy to raise child brides. Generally, child brides are sent to their future husband's families a few months after birth and raised by the in-laws from a young age, which is better treatment. If they are older, there is more likely to be emotional distance, and they are not treated as well as the family's own children, at least not as well as their own sons and daughters. Usually, when giving a daughter to someone as a child bride, they even have to subsidize them with dozens of yuan for living expenses. In Gansu's Western Road, the parents of child brides charge a dowry based on age at a rate of one yuan per year of age, which is already considered very unreasonable. But here, the bride's family even has to pay for living expenses, which is even more outrageous. In Lanxi and Jinhua, if daughters are lucky enough to grow up and get married in a palanquin woven by the "parents' orders and matchmaker's words," the old-fashioned etiquette can be very dizzying. For example, when the bride's family helps her into the palanquin, the mother cries with snot and tears, saying things like "Stepping on the stairs, step by step higher," "Give birth to a noble son and repay your mother's kindness." But at that time, the person helping the bride is afraid that if they are not careful, the bride's foot will step on the family's land, which would be unfavorable to the family. For the matchmakers and porters who come to greet the bride, even on extremely cold winter nights, they are not allowed to light a fire, fearing that it would harm the bride's family's wealth. With such superstitious contradictions, how can it be said to be marrying a "person"?

There is also the practice of "mortgaging wives" to others to have children. This evil custom of treating one's only wife as a sowing machine is most common in Qingtian, which belongs to the old Chuzhou (Lishui), and Dongyang in the Jinqu area. Because people who have property but no children and no possibility of taking a concubine come up with the idea of renting a wife to have children. The rent is a one-time payment of one hundred or ten yuan, or several tens of yuan per year for a period of three to five years. Whether the rented wife lives in your home or in her original husband's home is uncertain, but during this period, the ownership of the children born belongs to the person who paid for the wife's mortgage. As for those who mortgage their wives, it can be inferred that they are mostly families with many children who lack food and clothing. Although this is permitted by local customs, there is a different kind of bitterness in their hearts. Now, due to the development of transportation and the gradual opening of customs, the above-mentioned evil customs will naturally be gradually banned and eliminated.

The folk songs that are popular in each place usually fully and naturally reveal the people's thoughts, habits, and living conditions in that place. There are also many folk songs popular in various regions of Lanxi. Here are a few selected:

(1) At the age of ten, I married a seven-year-old boy. During the day, I dress him and send him to school. At night, I take off his shoes and socks and carry him to bed. He sleeps at my head, without discussion. After sleeping, I'm afraid the rats will carry him over the wall. Long bamboo poles for drying clothes, short bamboo poles for writing articles. I don't blame my grandfather, I don't blame my mother, I don't blame the little boy, I blame my own bad fate. I can only weep secretly until dawn.

(2) Big sparrow, long tail. Married a wife and forgot my mother. Early son, early profit. Early wife, early anger.

(3) One son, worry and fear. Two sons, icing on the cake. Three sons become four families. More sons and more daughters, more grievances. (This is the reality, but mostly due to the poison of inheritance.) One son and one daughter, a flower. No sons and no daughters, like immortals.

(4) January, accompany guests. February, weed wheat. March, go hungry. April, have wheat to grind. May, suffer. June, rice to the belly. July, fan. August, opera. September, drag shoes. October, grab firewood. November, suffer anger. December, be emperor. (This is a sketch of a farmer's life throughout the year, but "be emperor" does not mean a fat year, it is a euphemism for "avoiding debts.")

(5) Daughter dear, but not dear. A full dowry is still considered light. Son dear, but not dear. Three sentences and his face turns west. Husband and wife dear, but not dear. Same bed, same quilt, two minds. Brothers dear, but not dear. One bowl brought, one bowl invited. Only copper coins and silver are truly dear. Use them whenever you need to go.

(6) Three people, one heart, gold everywhere. (The effect of cooperation is like this. Don't laugh at the old farmer's ignorance.)

Page 10

Expansion of the Japanese Army in North China

Reorganization Implemented on August 1st, Tokuwo Watanabe Appointed Chief of Staff

Tianjin dispatch: Since Wanichiro Tashiro took office as the commander of the Japanese North China Garrison, its organization has been strengthened due to the increase in troops. The commander is of the rank of lieutenant general, and the chief of staff is of the rank of major general. The current chief of staff, Toshihide Nagami, is officially a colonel. According to custom, he will either be promoted or transferred, and a new officer will be appointed by the Japanese military headquarters to replace him. It was rumored a month ago that Nagami would be promoted to major general during the regular troop movements in August and remain in his original position. However, it has recently been learned that this is not accurate. Nagami belongs to the far-left faction of young officers, and his political views often differ from those of Tashiro and some members of the Japanese military headquarters. Tashiro wants to effectively direct operations, so he wants Nagami transferred. Tokuwo Watanabe, head of the Second Department of the Japanese General Staff Headquarters, came to negotiate the matter, with an accompanying mission being to change the chief of staff. After Watanabe returns home and reports, the matter will be largely decided. Watanabe will succeed as chief of staff. Nagami, due to his familiarity with the situation in North China, will be transferred to the post of director of the Japanese special service agency in Taiyuan, remaining in North China. The Japanese military headquarters recently felt that the authority of the Japanese North China Garrison should be increased and the organization should be improved. Therefore, it simultaneously ordered that the organization be modeled after the Japanese Kwantung Army, with seven departments under the commander: staff, adjutant, manager, translator, military doctor, veterinarian, and economic advisor. The staff department is divided into three sections and an intelligence system. Iida Yasujiro, the current senior staff officer of the Japanese North China Garrison, will serve as the head of the First Section. Kazuji Wachi, the current director of the Taiyuan special service agency, will be transferred to the post of head of the Second Section. He will be promoted to colonel during the regular troop movements in August. The head of the Third Section has not yet been determined and will be a colonel-level officer familiar with the situation in North China, dispatched by the Japanese Ministry of the Army. The original senior staff officer, Yoshie Ishii, will be transferred to the General Staff Headquarters in Japan. The original staff officer of the garrison, Yoshihide Hayashi (head of the investigation team), will be transferred to Shanghai to serve as an assistant military attaché at the embassy. The adjutant department will have communications and investigation teams, also headed by senior officers. The official announcement can be made at the end of this month and implemented on August 1st. This is slightly different from the previous organization. The commander of the Japanese North China Garrison now has the ability to independently exercise military power.

The Greater Asia Association, organized by General Iwane Matsui, advocates the so-called unity of East Asian nations and joint defense against the eastward advance of white people. A branch has been established in Tianjin. When the puppet autonomous movement was rampant, the association planned to hold a meeting in Dalian to promote autonomy. However, because it was unsuccessful, Matsui has now sent the association's director, Shumei Okawa, to Nanyang and the Philippines to contact local people and reopen a Greater Asia National Congress. The location will be in Beiping or Tianjin. Representatives from Manchukuo and Hebei-East Hebei will participate. Okawa is about to finish his activities in Nanyang and will return to Dalian at the end of the month. He will first hold a preparatory meeting in Dalian and come to Tianjin in early June to contact all parties. If the circumstances allow, the meeting can be convened in September or October of this year. (17th)

Japanese Merchants Invest in North China's Industries

Mitsui and Other Foreign Firms Deeply Affected by Smuggling, Plan to Jointly Operate Factories in Tianjin; Baocheng Yarn Factory Auctioned Off to Japanese Merchants

Tianjin dispatch: Smuggling by ronin in North China is considered a source of distress and pain even by legitimate merchants in their own country. However, this is one of the strategies in the larger sense of policy, and legitimate merchants have to endure their sufferings in silence. It has recently been learned that the Mitsui and Mitsubishi firms, as well as the Okura Company, were originally giant import and export trading houses, whose monthly sales of goods in North China averaged more than 1.3 million yuan. Since the rampant smuggling, all legitimate commodities imported by these firms have been piled up in warehouses and cannot be sold. The volume of trade has plummeted from the thaw of the Dagu port in March to the present, falling to about 200,000 yuan per month. The trading firms are almost unable to sustain themselves. In fact, the smuggling life is not decent, and they cannot imitate it, so they can only let themselves suffer losses. Recently, the firms have realized that if things continue in this way, their business will come to a standstill. Therefore, they convened a special meeting and decided to adopt a joint business approach. All artificial silk, piece goods, soda water, porcelain, glass, beer, and other items that need to be imported with high tariffs will be manufactured locally in factories in Tianjin and Yu, saving on tariffs and freight costs. The cost will be lower, which can compete with smuggled goods. This will also save face for the three firms. Currently, the selected sites are mostly rented vacant land on both sides of the Hai River in the Chengtangzhuang and Guajiasi areas in the suburbs of Tianjin, and construction will begin in the shortest time. Among them, Mitsubishi is more experienced in running a glass factory and may create one independently, starting construction ahead of the others. According to their investigation, there are thirteen glass factories in Tianjin, including Yaohua, but their capital is not strong and their products are not of high quality. If they invest 500,000 yuan to set up a factory, they will surely be able to reap great profits. Even if Chinese-run factories do not resist, it will be difficult for them to survive.

Shanzhong, the director of the Shanzhong Iron and Steel Plant in Shenyang, came to North China to investigate a month ago and learned that the sales of aluminum-zinc iron sheets (i.e., iron tiles) required by the construction industry in North China are very good. Therefore, he contacted the South Manchuria Railway Company to obtain its assistance in setting up a branch factory in Tianjin. He has already purchased 1,500 mu of private land near the Yuda Spinning Factory in Xiaoliuzhuang, downstream of the Hai River, and construction will begin next month. The project will be completed by November at the latest, and the first batch of goods can be produced by the end of the year. The minimum production capacity is 1,500 tons per month. The current Tianjin market sells 200 to 300 tons per month. In the future, the factory will contact the Okura and Mitsui firms to promote sales, with a minimum of 300 tons per month. In six or seven months, sales can reach 500 to 600 tons. It is said that the factory will also manufacture enamel porcelain. If the business is successful, the British and German commercial markets in North China can be replaced.

Since the news of the sale of the Huaxin Yarn Factory spread, the Japanese companies Xingzhong, Okura, Da-Nippon Spinning, Kanebo, and Toyo Spinning have all been in contact to buy it. Huaxin demanded that regardless of who buys it, they must sign an agreement guaranteeing that workers cannot be laid off for at least six months and that staff cannot be laid off for at least three months before other issues can be discussed. Therefore, all buyers considered this a prerequisite for the purchase. Currently, they are discussing the matter. The Huaxin shareholders intend to hold an auction in the same way that the Baocheng Yarn Factory was sold, starting with a minimum price of 1.2 million yuan, allowing buyers to openly compete. It is scheduled to be implemented at the end of the month. The factory has more than 2,000 workers. It is said that after hearing about the factory's sale, they were all panicked and sent representatives to the Bureau of Social Affairs to petition, saying that the factory was not losing money and that some shareholders wanted to sell it to foreigners due to disagreements among the shareholders. They asked the authorities to send someone to investigate and prohibit them from selling it to foreigners to avoid oppression of the Chinese yarn factory. The Bureau of Social Affairs has agreed to investigate. As for the Baocheng Yarn Factory, it went bankrupt due to excessive foreign debt. Recently, shareholders asked creditors to liquidate it and then sell it. Any surplus would be returned to shareholders proportionally. After the liquidation by the banking creditor group, no one bought it for a while. Therefore, it was publicly auctioned at the Xinhua Building in the French Concession on the 16th. The Japanese trading houses Yuda, Okura, and Kanebo Spinning competed to buy it. The Yuda Yarn Factory, which was run by the Japanese and was closed down, was sold for 1.37 million yuan. The procedures will be completed next week. Yuda plans to start work in September and will be named a branch factory. The factory will now fulfill its 40,000-spindle ambition. Baocheng has 25,000 spindles and the machinery is older than that of Huaxin and Yuda. It owes more than 2 million in foreign debt. This sale will use the proceeds to repay the creditors proportionally. The shareholders will only be relieved of their debts. (Hai 18th)

Second Phase of the Lu-Huang Canal Intermodal Project, Adding Irrigation Tunnels to Drain Water from the Canal's West Slope, Economic Commission Allocates 180,000 Yuan to Assist

Jinan dispatch: The Shandong Huang Canal intermodal project previously received an appropriation of 260,000 yuan from the National Economic Commission and 110,000 yuan from the province itself. All projects, such as the Weijiashan pumping station and the Zhougong River irrigation tunnel, have been decisively underway. Now, the Huang Canal intermodal project office believes that the first phase of the project is about to be completed and the second phase of the project should be prepared for. However, the original project plan only focused on navigation due to budget cuts. The irrigation tunnels for draining water from the canal's west slope were not built. Now, after the Huang Canal intermodal project office conducted an on-site survey of the terrain, they believed that if the irrigation tunnels are not built, the canal water will be high and slope water will not be able to enter the canal. If the canal water level is lowered as much as possible to allow slope water to enter the canal, the canal water will be shallow, which will hinder navigation. For the sake of both flood control and navigation, it is necessary to build irrigation tunnels. In addition to the two irrigation tunnels that have already been built in the Zhougong River, 14 more irrigation tunnels need to be added. Three tunnels need to be built at the intersection of the south branch of the Tuohai River and the Si River, three tunnels at the intersection of the north branch of the Tuohai River and the canal, one tunnel at the intersection of the north branch of the Majia River and the canal, and two tunnels at Zhang Guantang. Including the repair of three bridges and supervision fees, the total cost is 256,892 yuan in national currency. However, the province's financial resources are insufficient to allocate funds. The flood control project cannot be carried out. Although navigation can be勉强carried out, the waterlogging along the canal will inevitably be difficult to avoid. Therefore, they immediately drafted the second phase of the project plan, charts, and budget, and submitted them to the Department of Construction, which forwarded them to the National Economic Commission, requesting that this fund be included in the water conservancy project budget for the 25th year and continue to be allocated to avoid 工亏一篑.

The Department of Construction received the charts from the Huang Canal intermodal project office and deemed the addition of irrigation tunnels to drain water from the canal's west slope to be extremely important. There were some discrepancies in the proposed second phase of the project plan and budget. Therefore, it immediately sent a letter to the Yellow River Conservancy Commission and forwarded it to the National Economic Commission, requesting permission to include it in the water conservancy project budget for the 25th year and allocate funds to facilitate the project. It is now learned that this fund was approved at the National Water Conservancy Conference held in Beijing on the 16th, and 180,000 yuan will be allocated to assist. With this assistance, the second phase of the Huang Canal intermodal project will be able to continue to be completed. (17th)

Kunshan: Deputy Captain Gao Transferred to Wu County

Zong Han, the deputy captain of the 9th Security Brigade stationed in Kunshan, has served for more than four years. On the 18th, he received an order from the province to be transferred to the 7th Security Brigade in Wu County. The vacant position will be filled by Zhu Huang. It is learned that Gao will leave for Suzhou to take up his new post after the newly appointed Deputy Captain Zhu comes to Kunshan to complete the handover.

The facilities of the county's prisons and detention centers need more attention. In order to improve the government, the county government is preparing to organize a Prison Improvement Association, with the heads of various agencies and organizations as members and County Magistrate Peng Baichuan as the chairman. After active preparations, it has been established.

Changshu: Mass Literacy Class Graduates

The mass literacy class sponsored by the 14 towns in the first district here has completed its four-month training period. The first class held a joint graduation ceremony at Xiaoyao You this morning, the 18th. Various sectors donated many prizes, which were personally awarded and distributed by the county magistrate. It is learned that this first class had a total of 39 classes with 1,132 students. At the same time, it can be known that in the past four months, the first district has added more than 1,100 literate people. Therefore, the graduation ceremony was solemn. In addition to the speeches by the county magistrate and district chief, student representatives gave responses. The awards were given and the event ended at 11:00 AM.

Nanhui: Robbery of Cigarettes Solved

In order to expand its business, the Shanghai Yongtaihe Cigarette Company recently sent a team to Pudong to sell cigarettes such as Lao Dao and Xiannv. Unexpectedly, they encountered a robbery in the Huangpu River a few days ago, and 39 boxes of cigarettes were stolen. The team reported the incident to the Jianghai Customs Water Police Station for investigation. Three suspects, Gu Sanlang and others, were arrested. They confessed that they conspired with Zhang Cailin of Jiajialong, Zhoupu Town, and Shen Jialu of Beicai Town, both in the fifth district of this county. Chief Detective Cheng Yongnian, Detective Gu Wenkui, and six others were dispatched to Zhoupu, together with Sun Yunda, the patrol officer of the Public Security Sub-Station in the town, to arrest Zhang Cailin. They then went to Beicai and arrested Shen Jialu. They also learned that the stolen goods were hidden in the home of Pan Shukui in Xiukang Township. When the detectives went to Pan's house, Pan was not there, but they found 25 boxes of the original stolen cigarettes in the tomb house of Dai Zhenchang, east of Pan's house. Yesterday, the people and stolen goods were escorted to the county for investigation.

Jiashan: Smuggling Intercepted at Fengjing Station

On the 12th, Fengjing East Station intercepted 200 bags of smuggled fertilizer from Shanghai, worth more than 5,000 yuan. The brands include Hengfeng (117 bags), Gongfeng (28 bags), Haisenji (20 bags), and other brands (more than 30 bags).

Expediting Deed Tax Collection

The county government believes that property owners often delay reporting taxes after acquiring property, which greatly affects tax revenue. It has ordered the director of the Joint Office for Township Construction in the First District in Xiangfeng to also serve as the deed tax collection officer for the entire county. Each township will hire assistant collection officers in their respective areas to strictly investigate and report. They will be rewarded with a percentage of the fines collected. In order to facilitate property owners in reporting taxes, specific flexible measures have been determined: (1) If the grain string is not brought during the registration of the deed, but the name of the original grain payer is recorded in the deed, verification with the register should be allowed for tax reporting. (2) Land that has been missed or is outside the boundary should be reported voluntarily in accordance with the Qingzhang method, and one year of grain tax should be allowed to be paid retroactively.

Jiangyin: Garrison Executes Traitors

The 87th Division of the garrison successively arrested three traitors, Li Huaqing, He Shugao (from Taixing, unemployed), and Zhao Guangshun (from Yangzhou, street performer), in its defense area. They confessed to infiltrating the defense area to侦察military information. At about 10:00 AM on the 18th, they were escorted to Junsan, outside the north gate, and executed by shooting in accordance with military law.

Preparing for County Hospital

The Department of Civil Affairs ordered County Magistrate Yuan to convert the existing Opium Treatment Center into a county hospital within a short period. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Yuan began preparations and the Administrative Council decided that the hospital will be located at the original site of the Opium Treatment Center (Guanyue Temple). On the 17th, the Department of Civil Affairs appointed Shi Zizhu, the director of the Opium Treatment Center, as the director of the preparatory committee for the county hospital.

Russian Opportunistic Theft

North Outer City Walls: At approximately 4 PM on the 17th, three Russian nationals, men and women, arrived in a small car at Baochang Grain and Tobacco Shop outside the north city walls. They attempted to purchase cigarettes, offering a ten-yuan Central Bank note and requesting change specifically in five-yuan and four one-yuan notes. The shop, lacking the requested denominations, suggested exchanging the note at Wang Qiaji Rice Mill. The Russians proceeded to the rice mill, but it also lacked Central Bank notes. The Russians then picked through the bills at the mill, taking their original note back. Afterward, it was discovered that forty-five yuan in Central Bank notes was missing. A pursuit was immediately launched, but the Russians had already fled in their car.

Zhenjiang: Battle Between Soldiers and Bandits in Dalu Town

A soldier from the county security team in Dalu Town, Fifth District of the county, noticed a suspicious-looking individual on the street the other day and reported it to his unit. Platoon Leader Tao led a team to investigate. Upon realizing they were discovered, the bandit and his gang opened fire, resisting arrest. The troops immediately returned fire, and a battle ensued for several minutes. One bandit was killed on the spot, and a box gun was seized. A search was then conducted along the Xin'gang River, where a small boat was discovered, along with another box gun, over one hundred packs of cigarettes, and several bolts of cloth. One bandit and two boatmen were subsequently captured. After interrogation, they confessed to the robbery. The county government, in addition to rigorously pursuing the escaped bandits, has handed over the suspects, stolen goods, and weapons to the garrison command for further investigation.

Yangzhou: Dismissal of Security Training Officers

The Fifth District of Jiangsu Province Security Training Commissioner's Office and the squad leader training class have both been ordered to close simultaneously. It is understood that Training Officer Yan Ming has been transferred to the Provincial Security Department as a service member.

Request to Establish a Public Health Experiment Zone

The county government of this county believes that Yangzhou City has a high concentration of smokers, and the urban area is exceptionally vast, with a population reaching 120,000. All aspects of healthcare and epidemic prevention require significant funding, which the economic resources of a single county cannot possibly fully support. Moreover, Yangzhou City is separated from the provincial capital by only a narrow strip of water, and is close to Jingkou (Zhenjiang), with officials frequently traveling between Yangzhou and Zhenjiang. Public health is undoubtedly a matter of public image. Recognizing this, the county government recently submitted a request to the Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs for approval to follow the precedents of the public health experiment zones in Huaiyin and Jianbi Town in Zhenjiang, and establish a public health experiment zone in the urban area of this county.

Nantong: Security Team Conscription Training

The security teams of various counties in the Nantong region have gradually disbanded their hired recruits and replaced them with conscripts, with considerable success. As the period for this year's discharge of veterans approaches, the county government has dispatched Section Chief Wang Youwen and others to various districts to instruct the conscription of strong young men in preparation for forming teams to replace them. Peng Longxiang, Deputy Commander of the District Security Command, is also inspecting the rural areas.

Suppression of Bandits Through Clean-Up Campaign

During this clean-up campaign in Nantong, the military police arrested male and female bandits, all of whom were sent to the District Security Command. Due to the large number of people, the military judge conducted trials. Those with serious offenses were detained pending punishment, while over twenty ordinary thieves were transferred to the court.

Gaoyou: Bicycle Registration Implemented

The county government, noting that the roads in the city and suburbs of this county have all been repaired and are smooth, and that the number of bicycles has increased sharply, with frequent reports of unskilled riders injuring pedestrians, has therefore implemented registration and licensing in accordance with the bicycle management regulations of the Construction Department to facilitate management. It has been decided that before 12:00 noon on the 21st of this month, owners of bicycle shops and private bicycle owners should obtain registration forms from the Construction Section of the county government (i.e., the Third Section). Before 12:00 noon on the 23rd, they should bring their bicycles to the front of the county government auditorium to await inspection. Those who pass will be issued magnetic license plates (at 2 jiao each) and assigned numbers. They should then pay the donation fee to the local donation collection office at any time. The fee is one yuan per quarter for commercial bicycles and five jiao for private bicycles. It is reported that there are approximately 200 bicycles in this county.

Jiaxing: Smuggled Goods Discovered in Cloth Factory

The Jiahe Cloth Factory in Jiaxing has been in operation for over twenty years and has had some success in the past. Recently, wealthy merchants such as Bao Jiezhi have taken over its operation. They have reduced wages, and a strike occurred last month. It was only after the party and government made strenuous efforts to mediate that work was resumed. However, it was discovered that the factory had imported a large quantity of smuggled goods the other day. Someone secretly reported this to the county government and provided detailed drawings. The county government immediately ordered the head of the detective team, Shen Jianfei, detective Li Zhankui, and other detectives to search the factory on the afternoon of the 18th, based on the drawings. They discovered twenty-two boxes of bleaching powder and over one thousand packages of "Laifeng" brand Japanese yarn. The discovered items were reported to County Magistrate Wang and sealed pending further investigation. However, according to Zhou Yuqing, the manager of the factory, the bleaching powder was purchased from the Yuanyuhe Color Material Shop in Shanghai at a price of 3 yuan 6 jiao per box and was delivered by the Tiansheng Transportation Company on Tangwan Street on the 14th. The Japanese yarn was shipped from a cloth factory in Shanghai to be woven into cloth and was not smuggled goods. However, the public is paying close attention to this matter. As the county's anti-smuggling association is being established, the discovery of this situation will be severely punished as an example to others.

Hangzhou: Subsidy for Tea Industry Improvement

The Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, in order to improve Pingshui green tea, has established the Pingshui Tea Industry Improvement Field. The operating expenses of 28,000 yuan will be subsidized by half by the National Economic Council's Agricultural Department. Recently, the department was merged into the Ministry of Industry, but the subsidy of 14,000 yuan will still be allocated by the Economic Council. In addition, the Ministry of Industry will allocate a guidance fee of 8,000 yuan for technical improvement. The Field is scheduled to be established in early August, with Wu Juenong internally designated as the director.

Fundraising for Oil Material Factory

The Ministry of Industry is planning to establish a vegetable oil material factory, and Zhejiang Province has decided to invest 300,000 yuan. 150,000 yuan will be allocated by the Finance Department in the form of newly issued government bonds as official shares, and the remaining 150,000 yuan will be raised from commercial shares. Finance Minister Cheng Yuanfan will go to Shanghai in the next few days to encourage tung oil merchants to invest, in order to raise the funds as soon as possible and submit them to the Ministry for approval. The establishment meeting of the factory is scheduled to be held soon. Construction Minister Wu Tingyang went to Beijing for this reason and will return to Hangzhou soon.

Preparation for Literature Exhibition

In order to promote provincial culture and improve academic atmosphere, the Zhejiang Department of Education has decided to hold a Zhejiang Literature Exhibition during the Double Tenth Festival this year. The Provincial Library is responsible for organizing the exhibition, drafting various regulations, and organizing a working committee. Zhang Pengnian, the third section chief of the Department of Education, and Chen Xunci, the director of the Provincial Library, will serve as the director and deputy director, respectively. The General Library on Daxue Road will be the venue. Scholars who are enthusiastic about culture and education, and famous collectors from both inside and outside the province, will be hired as design committee members. Wang Fuchuan, Yu Yueyuan, Qian Junfu, Sun Licai, and Shao Peizi have been designated as standing committee members. After discussions, Sun Churen and Xiang Lansheng have been hired as the director and deputy director of the book group, Yuan Siyong and Gao Yehou as the director and deputy director of the calligraphy and painting group, Zou Jingshu and Ye Pinsan as the director and deputy director of the ancient artifact group, Chen Boheng and Gu Dingmei as the director and deputy director of the bronze and stone rubbing group, Wang Fuchuan and Li Chukuang as the director of the revolutionary literature group, and Lin Fengmian and Chen Wanli as the director of the picture group. In accordance with the branch rules, the administrative inspectors of each district will serve as the directors, and local famous scholars will serve as the deputy directors. Branch offices for collecting items will also be established in Nanjing and Shanghai, and negotiations are currently underway.

Pinghu: Wrongful Killing of Refugee Case in Quan Gong

Regarding the case of Zhang Afu, a member of the Quan Gong Pavilion militia, mistakenly killing a refugee from Hubei, it is reported that the county government originally scheduled an autopsy on the 16th to examine the bullet casing. However, because the case requires forensic examination, a request has been submitted to the High Court to send officials to Pinghu to preside over the investigation. Meanwhile, the request of the parties concerned to temporarily postpone the autopsy has been approved.

Bengbu: Last Year's Salt Tax Revenue

Bengbu is the distribution center for Huai salt, and the salt supply comes from Banpu and other fields in northern Anhui. It is transported by truck, sea, and river. The city is a hub for truck, sea, and river transportation, so there are many salt warehouses, making it a large salt market. The salt consumption areas of 19 counties in northern Anhui and 14 counties in eastern Henan are distributed and sold from here. In recent years, salt has also been directly transported to Guzhen and Mingguang, and sold together with Bengbu salt. For truck and sea salt transported to Guzhen and Mingguang, a local market tax of 4 yuan per dan, a military tax and sales tax of 2 yuan, and a building tax of 1 jiao are collected on the spot. For salt transported to Bengbu, a market carrying fee is collected first, and then officials from the tax collection office collect the military and sales tax of 2 yuan at the salt warehouse when the salt is unloaded. The military and sales tax for river salt is collected at Xiba. Since Bengbu is the only major salt market on the Anhui-Henan border, the Huai River Salt Affairs Supervisory Office has established a tax collection office here to collect the military and sales tax on northern salt. In the twenty-fourth fiscal year, from July of last year to June of this year, a total of 1,388,313 dan of salt were transported by truck, sea, and river. The tax collection office collected a total of 2,352,261 yuan in salt tax. Recently, newly taxed salt transported by merchants has been loaded onto ships for sale. It is expected that the salt tax revenue for the twenty-fifth fiscal year will increase compared to the previous year.

Local News

European and Asian Giant Aircraft Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

Sino-German Aviation Achieves Fourth Success: Chinese and Foreign Guests Attend Welcome Ceremony Enthusiastically; German Community in Shanghai Holds Grand Tea Party to Welcome; Another Aircraft Continues Flight to China and Expected to Arrive in the Next Few Days

The Junkers Ju 52 tri-motor giant aircraft, leased by Eurasia Aviation Corporation from Germany for the fourth time, was flown from Berlin to China by famous German aviator Lutz and others. It arrived in Shanghai at 1:15 PM yesterday and landed at Longhua Airport. This is the fourth successful direct flight between China and Germany. Therefore, yesterday, over a hundred Chinese and foreign guests attended the welcome ceremony. The German community also held a grand tea party to welcome the aircraft, and the atmosphere was very enthusiastic. The details are as follows:

Airport Arrangement

After receiving the telegram from the company that the aircraft had arrived in Hong Kong the day before yesterday, the company sent letters to various circles in China and abroad, inviting them to send representatives to participate in the welcome ceremony. At the same time, they sent representatives to Longhua Airport to arrange everything. The welcome ceremony venue was set up in the company's newly completed hangar. The national flags of China and Germany and the Eurasia Company flag were hung from the roof. In addition to the giant aircraft and a small fast aircraft parked in the hangar, several large dining tables were placed in front of the giant aircraft, surrounded by chairs. Fresh flowers and champagne were provided on the tables, as well as tea, snacks, and cold drinks to entertain the guests. The arrangement was simple and neat.

Welcome Guests

Yesterday was Sunday, and many guests attended the welcome ceremony. In addition to the company's general manager, Li Jingcong, who was unable to attend due to business in Beijing, those who attended included Walther, the representative of Lufthansa in China; Nolimo, the director of the Eastern Department of the German National Socialist Party; Stass, the representative of the Junkers Aircraft Factory in Shanghai; Weitman, the president of the German General Association; He En, the head of the aviation group of Eurasia Company; Miao Guanxuan, the director of the operations group; officials from the German Consulate; and over a hundred Chinese and German male and female guests. They were warmly received by Miao Guanxuan, Ling Yizhi, Wang Yanyun, and Cai Zhiren of the company.

Landing Situation

At 12:30 PM yesterday, Chinese and foreign guests arrived at the airport one after another. They were accompanied by company staff to visit the new hangar. At 1:15 PM, the giant aircraft was spotted in the eastern sky. One minute later, it reached the sky above the airport. The sound of the engines rumbled, shaking the entire airport. The welcomers applauded or took off their hats to express their welcome. The aircraft circled once in the sky, then flew to the Bund area and circled once before returning to the airport at 1:30 PM and landing safely in front of the large hangar. The aircraft's body was silver-gray and was a Junkers Ju 52. The fuselage was marked "D-Amar," and the tail was painted with the red swastika emblem of the German National Socialist Party. All speed, safety equipment, and seating were identical to the previous three aircraft.

Flower Presentation Welcome

After the aircraft landed, He En, the head of the aviation group, Miao Guanxuan, the director of the operations group, and Chinese and foreign guests crowded forward, surrounding the aircraft. Shortly after, the door opened, and the chief pilot, Lutz, the co-pilot, La'aiting, and the radio operator, Qiao Aide, all smiled and disembarked amid cheers. Except for Lutz, who was wearing a yellow flight suit, the rest were wearing white aviation suits. Miss Ye Shulian presented flowers to each of them separately, and they took a group photo with the welcoming guests next to the aircraft. They then went to the hangar to drink champagne together. Miao Guanxuan delivered a welcome speech on behalf of Li Jingcong, saying, "General Manager Li Jingcong is in Beijing on business, so I am representing Eurasia Company to express our welcome to everyone. Lufthansa has leased three giant aircraft, and this is the fourth one. We are very grateful for this spirit of cooperation. This spirit is sufficient to enhance Sino-German relations. We hope to achieve the goal of Sino-German air transportation based on this spirit and develop air traffic between China and Germany. I offer champagne to wish you all good health." After the speech, tea and snacks were served, and the event dispersed at around 2:00 PM. The pilots then went to the Broadway Mansion on the Waibaidu Bridge to rest.

Flight Details

After the aircraft arrived in Shanghai, Eurasia Company held a tea party at the German General Association at 454 Haige Road at 5:30 PM yesterday to entertain pilot Lutz and other members of the Chinese and German press. Pilot Lutz, La'aiting, Mrs. Lutz, and reporters from German newspapers, the Continental Daily, and Chinese newspapers attended. They were warmly received by Walder, the head of the aviation group of the company, and Secretary Ling Yizhi. During the party, pilot Lutz spoke to the Chinese and foreign reporters about his flight from Germany to China. When his vacation expired last December and he was preparing to come to China, he received a telegram from the Eurasia authorities requesting him to lease a giant aircraft and drive it. Although he had already purchased a boat ticket for the trip, he cancelled the passage and was pleased to accept the piloting duty. His goal was to complete this international long-distance flight mission. (Note: Lutz had previously flown a small single-engine aircraft from Germany to China via Dihua three years ago, so he has experience in long-distance flights.) After receiving the telegram in early June, he inspected the aircraft's components and test-flew it in Germany. He was very satisfied with it and began preparing to come to China. On the morning of July 5, at 6:30 AM, he piloted the aircraft and took off from Berlin's largest airport, Tempeihof. On the first day, he landed in Belgrade to refuel. That day, he flew to Rhodos, an island in the Mediterranean Sea, and spent the night there. When he was about to take off on the second day, there was a heavy rainstorm. After the rain stopped, the two mechanics who were traveling with him climbed onto the left and right wings to check the aircraft's components. Unfortunately, one of the mechanics slipped and fell to the ground. He was rushed to an Italian doctor for treatment, who diagnosed a serious injury with a broken leg bone. Lutz then flew the injured mechanic back to Athens, the capital of Greece, and sent him to a hospital for treatment. He also sent a telegram to Lufthansa in Berlin to report the incident and requested them to send another mechanic to replace him. He introduced Qiao Aide, who had worked in China for many years, as a mechanic because he was familiar with the Sino-German route and was capable of handling everything. Therefore, he went to Berlin to wait for Qiao to arrive in Athens, which delayed the journey for several days. Qiao finally arrived in Athens on July 13. On the morning of the 14th, he departed from Athens. He originally did not intend to go to Rhodos again, but had to land there to return the stretcher that carried the injured mechanic. After taking off from the island, he stopped in Aleppo to refuel, and then flew to Baghdad. On the 15th, he refueled in Buschir and flew to Jask in Persia, where he stayed for one day before flying directly to Karachi in India. The next day (the 16th), he departed from there and refueled in Johdpur and Alshadad. That night, he arrived in Caluta and spent the night. On the morning of the 17th, he departed from Caluta, refueled in Yangon, and then flew to Bangkok in Siam. On the 18th, he flew to Hanoi in Annam and then to Hong Kong. On the morning of the 19th (yesterday), at 7:30 AM, he took off from Hong Kong and finally flew to Shanghai Longhua Airport at 1:15 PM, completing this long-distance flight. He was very pleased. The actual total time of this trip was 57 hours of flight in the air, and 4 hours of delay due to the accident in Athens. The weather was good along the way from Germany to China, and the aircraft's components were fortunately not damaged. The flight was smooth. At each stop, the local Chinese and German people and consuls came to the station to take care of him and welcome him, for which he was deeply grateful. According to his original plan, he had planned to fly directly to Kunming, Yunnan, without going through Hong Kong, but because the Kunming airport was not good, he received a telegram from the Eurasia authorities on Friday instructing him to change his route and go through Hong Kong. When he departed from Hong Kong to fly to Shanghai, the weather was extremely bad, with heavy rain that obscured his direction. After careful driving, he circled low over the sea in Hong Kong several times before daring to fly directly to Shanghai in the right direction, which was a great fortune in misfortune, he said. After Lutz finished his report, Eurasia colleagues hosted a banquet for Lutz at the German General Association at 9:00 PM, where they raised their glasses and enjoyed themselves until they dispersed.

Joining the Route

According to the head of the company's aviation group, after the giant aircraft is left in Shanghai to be inspected and repaired, it will soon join the Shaanxi-Yunnan route for flight. In the future, it is planned to be deployed on the Lanzhou-Baotou route, because at present, there is only one small single-engine aircraft on the Lanzhou-Baotou route, and it is quite necessary to add a giant three-engine aircraft.

Another Aircraft Arrives Soon

According to the company's spokesperson, the company has leased two giant aircraft from Lufthansa this time. In addition to the one that arrived in Shanghai yesterday, the other one has already taken off from Berlin to China and is expected to arrive in Shanghai in the next few days. The aircraft will be assigned to various routes for application. The pilots who arrived in Shanghai yesterday, except for Lutz, who was originally employed by the company, the co-pilot, La'aiting, and the radio operator, Gao Aide, do not plan to return to Germany and will work at Eurasia Company.

Factory Federation: Preventing Smuggled Goods

Six Articles in Letter to Members

The Chinese National Products Manufacturers Association, recognizing that the dumping of smuggled goods endangers the foundation of the country, has issued a notice to all manufacturer members nationwide, warning them of six things, urging them to report smuggled goods, and improve manufacturing. The notice is recorded below. For the matter of notice, at this time of strong neighbor's aggression, political and economic oppression are increasing day by day. If we do not try to remedy the situation immediately, the foundation of the country will be destroyed, and it will be difficult to survive. Since the September 18th Incident, the Chinese people have been alarmed and horrified by the strong neighbor's military occupation, and all have lamented the loss of sovereignty and the increasing loss of land. In fact, what we should be alarmed and vigilant about is not limited to this. Looking around the country, although it has not yet been completely controlled by the enemy, the impact of international trade dumping and the recent serious smuggling have caused unprecedented attacks on our national industry and commerce, and the national economy is even in danger of bankruptcy. Therefore, the whole country holds the belief of self-reliance and strives to resist smuggled goods closely. Our member manufacturers, taking the promotion of national goods and the recovery of rights and interests as their duty, should uphold the creed of saving the country with national goods and serve the society and the country at this serious juncture. Therefore, the following six items are prescribed, and it is hoped that our member manufacturers will jointly abide by them: (1) The raw materials for manufactured products should be based on the principle of using domestic products; (2) If there are no domestic products that can be purchased for the raw material paper, then it must be determined whether there is a customs tariff when importing the goods; (3) Manufacturers should supervise each other and unanimously refuse to use smuggled goods; (4) If there are any purchases of smuggled goods or other illegal acts, they may be reported to this association secretly, and the competent authorities will be requested to punish them; (5) Industry infighting should be avoided, and business ethics should be respected. They must not raise prices to create opportunities for foreign goods, nor can they devalue prices too much to destroy the same industry; (6) Manufacturing technology should be improved, so that consumers are happy to purchase them. The above six items are both to save the country and to save themselves. It is hoped that our member manufacturers will understand this meaning together and abide by it consistently. This notice is hereby issued.

Smuggled Goods Gradually Disappearing in This City

Authorities Strictly Suppressing; Southern Smuggling Not Easy; Smuggling Merchants Suffering Heavy Losses

Shen Shi News reports that since the Ministry of Finance ordered strict suppression of smuggling in North China, and established anti-smuggling investigation offices along the Pinghan and Jinpu Railways, and allocated customs officers to inspect sections, although smuggling of goods to the south has not stopped, it is gradually coming to an end. A reporter recently learned from business circles that smuggled goods from North China have been rarely seen in Shanghai recently. Because smuggling merchants imported a large number of goods by sea and land last year and hoarded them, the crackdown is now strict, sales are stagnant, and the supply has already exceeded the demand. Although artificial silk, white sugar, and cigarette paper have been imported in the past, merchants are mostly unwilling to purchase these goods, so their sales are very small. Smuggling merchants have suffered heavy losses and have been unable to support themselves. At the same time, the smuggling situation in North China is also gradually becoming unsustainable. Smuggling rogues are greedy for profit. Since they have been affected by the strict investigation and seizure by the authorities, their organization has become scattered. It is recently heard that most of the smuggled goods to the south are transported by sea, but they cannot be sold in Xuzhou, Jinan, Qingdao, and other places, so they are trying to transport them to Shaanxi and other places at reduced prices for sale. It is not easy to come south to Nanjing and Shanghai. Therefore, smuggled goods in Shanghai are gradually disappearing. It is expected that after the organization of the anti-smuggling investigation office along the Beijing-Shenyang Railway by the General Office of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Investigation Bureau is established, and the smuggled goods from eastern Hebei are intercepted, smuggling in North China can be eliminated soon.

The Guangdong Situation is About to be Resolved; Shanghai-Guangdong Commerce is Gradually Recovering

Freight Volume Increasing Compared to Before

Shanghai-Guangdong commerce had been stagnant for over a month. Ministry of Finance Stipulates Inspection Measures for Domestic Artificial Silk and Textile Products; Customs Sets Deadlines for Factories to Report and Verify Purchases of Artificial Silk, and to Obtain Customs Tax Receipts

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the Ministry of Finance, to prevent the smuggling of imported artificial silk and artificial silk textiles, had previously included them in the inspection list. However, domestic factories also produce artificial silk textiles, which had not been subject to inspection. Now, to prevent exploitation by unscrupulous merchants and avoid undermining the effectiveness of preventing the smuggling of artificial silk imports, it has stipulated nine inspection and inventory procedures for factories purchasing artificial silk and producing domestic textiles made of or mixed with artificial silk. These are excerpted below:

Customs Declaration, Inventory, and Issuance of Transportation and Sales Permits

(1) All domestic textiles made of or mixed with artificial silk by factories should be inspected in accordance with the provisional regulations for imported goods. Factories transporting and selling the aforementioned textiles without permits should be handled according to Article 8 of the provisional regulations for the inspection of imported goods. (2) Customs will set a deadline for factories to inventory their existing stock. (3) Factories should report the quantity of their existing stock to customs within the deadline set by customs, attaching a certificate from the relevant trade association. Customs will dispatch personnel to the factories for verification and registration. (4) Registered existing textile stocks will be exempted from tax certificates and issued transportation and sales permits. (5) For all registered existing artificial silk stocks, factories should provide proof of tax payment. If no proof of tax payment is available, customs will set a deadline for factories to request a tax payment certificate from the original importing customs and submit it for verification. Customs may temporarily seal the relevant stock of artificial silk. If the customs proof of tax payment is not submitted for verification after the deadline, the relevant factories should immediately pay the supplementary tax according to the import tariff, and will be exempt from penalties or confiscation.

Purchase of Raw Materials Must Include Tax Receipts

(6) All factories purchasing artificial silk raw materials should obtain evidence of paid import taxes from the artificial silk merchants selling the goods, provided by customs, and keep it for verification. Customs will issue transportation and sales permits for the artificial silk textiles reported by the factories based on the artificial silk tax payment evidence. (7) All factories purchasing artificial silk and selling artificial silk textiles should record detailed information in ledgers according to the provisional regulations for the inspection of goods transportation and sales and submit a monthly list, certified by the relevant trade association, to the nearby customs for inspection at any time. (8) All textiles mixed with artificial silk should be handled in accordance with these measures. (9) In areas with a large number of factories, customs will conduct the inventory. In other areas with fewer factories and far from customs, the relevant trade association (or the chamber of commerce if there is no trade association) will conduct the initial inventory and report the quantity of existing stock to the nearby customs, which will then dispatch personnel to verify and inventory. The above measures, when conducted by customs, must be handled by the tax commissioner and the customs superintendent in consultation with the trade association or chamber of commerce.

Taxes and Levies Similar to Income Tax

Must Be Abolished Universally to Avoid Public Concerns

According to Xin Xin News Agency, the Ministry of Finance's planned income tax is about to be levied. Various trade associations believe several clauses are of great importance to the national economy, the people's livelihood, and the future of industry, and have specifically submitted opinions to the central government for modification. Xin Xin News Agency reporters specifically interviewed economic experts and leading merchants to solicit their opinions. They all expressed support for the government's imposition of income tax, citing that income tax has been implemented in Europe and the United States for a long time and is regarded as a major national tax. The state's tax revenue should be direct, which can eliminate corruption and not harm the people. Currently, the major national taxes in our country, such as customs duties, salt taxes, and consolidated taxes, are not direct in nature. Not only is the burden on the people uneven, but the state's revenue is also inconvenient. Furthermore, the state budget is greatly related to direct and indirect tax revenue. Therefore, for the sake of strengthening the state's finances, for the people to fulfill their obligations, and for the sake of equitable tax burden, income tax is a good tax that benefits the national economy, the people's livelihood, and the development of industry, and it is essential to implement it quickly. In the past, our country's taxes were very complex. As a result of the efforts of the financial authorities to rectify them over the years, the types of arbitrary taxes and levies abolished are not few. However, in order to eliminate public concerns and the perception of double taxation, before the income tax is levied, it is necessary to thoroughly investigate the taxes in each province and city. If there are taxes and levies of the same nature, they must be abolished universally. Then the implementation of the income tax will certainly be very smooth.

Ministry of Finance Issues Nearly 10 Million Yuan in New Subsidiary Currency; Still Not Circulating in Remote Provinces and Being Promoted; One-Yuan and Half-Yuan New Coins Also Being Minted

Since implementing the legal tender policy, the Ministry of Finance has also sought to adjust the financial system and unify the subsidiary currency. Because they are convenient to carry and easy to calculate, people are happy to use them. Therefore, demand on the market has increased sharply, and the Central Mint is continuing to work overtime to mint them. During the summer of this year, the factory originally had a summer break, but due to the minting of the new subsidiary currency, it worked as usual. According to a Dagong News Agency reporter's inquiry to financial authorities, more than 9 million of this new currency has been minted to date, approaching 10 million yuan, and all of it has been circulated on the market. However, local authorities in various provinces need this new subsidiary currency urgently to adjust the financial market and have repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to ship it for use. Therefore, the new currency is in short supply. It is used extensively in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. It is not yet widespread in remote provinces due to insufficient distribution and is currently being vigorously promoted. As for the one-yuan coins and half-yuan subsidiary currency recently decided to be minted by the Ministry of Finance, their models have also been cast overseas and shipped to Shanghai. They are slightly larger but similar in style to the new currency. They are also about to be minted.

Allocating One-Fifth of Total Deposits

Although each bank has already expanded rural lending as much as possible, such as organizing the China Agricultural Loan Syndicate and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Spring Cocoon Collection Loan Syndicate to handle rural lending, the total amount of loans is still less than one-fifth of the total savings deposits. Therefore, each bank has decided to allocate one-fifth of the total savings deposits as joint funding for the Agricultural Foundation Bureau to comply with the Savings Bank Law.

New British Ambassador is Scheduled to Arrive in China

Around Mid-September

The newly appointed British Ambassador to China, Sir Hughe Montgomery Knatchbull-Hugessen, has now scheduled to depart from England on the Changxing Shipping Company's Empress of Canada on the 4th of next month, accompanied by his wife, son, staff, and others, to take up his new post in China. According to diplomatic sources here, Hugessen will disembark in Japan for a few days' stay, taking the opportunity to visit the political and social circles there. The date of his arrival in China is scheduled for mid-September. Hugessen is currently 51 years old, with one son and two daughters. He studied at Oxford University and entered the diplomatic service in 1908. In 1919, he served on the British delegation to the Paris Peace Conference and was soon promoted to the rank of First Secretary. From 1926 to 1930, he served as Counselor at the British Embassy in Belgium. From 1930 to 1934, he served as Minister to various countries in the Balkan Peninsula. Subsequently, he was transferred to the post of Minister to Iran. After the former Ambassador to China, Sir J. T. T. Babington, was transferred to the post of Permanent Under-Secretary, Hugessen was promoted to the post of Ambassador to China. Hugessen had previously visited China once and has always paid close attention to the situation in the Far East.

Joint Meeting of Shanghai Slum Representatives

Organizing a Slum United Association to Petition Various Parties on a Regular Basis

The slum dwellers in the two districts of Pudong and Puxi in the city, in order to seek effective communication and self-help, held a joint meeting of Pudong and Puxi slum representatives at Bing Society at 4 pm yesterday. It was decided to organize a slum united association, elect 29 preparatory committee members to be responsible for the preparations, and scheduled to petition various parties for relief on the 21st. The details are recorded as follows:

Representatives Present

The attendees yesterday included Chen Jiufeng, representative of the First Special District Citizens' Association; Tang Anping, Xu Xiguang, Sun Hankui, Guo Bingzhi, Chen Yongde, Zhang Ziying, Huang Maoxiang, Ye Shuting, Yao Shanfu, Chen Jingqing, Huang Zhizhong, representatives of the slums on Lan Road, Yanshan Road, and Chaoyang Road in Pudong District; Hu Yumen, Xu Yiqun, Sun Dongchen, Sun Weijin, Xu Xipeng, Liu Jinshan, Tian Rui, Gu Tiansheng, Yin Qingyu, Yin Youde, Jiang Yibo, Zhu Wenxue, Liu Guangchun, Li Jiaxuan, representatives of the slums on Seymour Road, Xiaoshadu Road, Tokyo Road, Yichang Road, and Mabailu Road in Puxi District; and more than 50 other people. Chen Jiufeng was elected chairman.

Chairman's Report

After the formalities, the chairman first reported that the Municipal Council recently planned to order the slums in the two districts of Pudong and Puxi to relocate immediately. Although a postponement of the demolition had been obtained as a result of discussions with Mr. Yu Qiaqing, a director of the Municipal Council, a proper and thorough solution for the slums had still not been provided. Therefore, it is hoped that everyone present today will jointly address the issue. It is hoped that everyone will unite and fight together to ensure that the Municipal Council has a place to resettle the slums before they are allowed to relocate. Otherwise, it would be inhumane to simply pursue the beautiful name of tidying up the city and disregarding the displacement of the slums. This association cannot but be moved and take action. Therefore, it is hoped that everyone will work together until the goal of self-help is achieved. Currently, a united association will first be formed by the slums in the two districts of Pudong and Puxi to decide on procedures and continue negotiations with the Municipal Council. My opinion is to: (1) expedite the construction of public housing so that the slums have a place to live; (2) increase labor remuneration and establish public factories; (3) leniently register rickshaw pullers; (4) the slums automatically organize a united association for systematic management; (5) limit the increase of slums; (6) automatically conduct household registration surveys; (7) implement baojia self-government, with every ten households as a group. These seven points are submitted to you today for discussion. It is hoped that everyone will express their opinions as much as possible in order to decide on the direction of action and achieve the goal of self-help.

Resolutions

(1) The motion to organize a slum united association was resolved and passed unanimously without objection. (2) The motion to stipulate the number of preparatory committee members for the slum united association was resolved and 29 representatives from the two districts of Pudong and Puxi were elected as preparatory committee members to be responsible for the preparations. (3) The motion that the association should request relief from the Municipal Council, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and other parties was resolved. It was approved that on the 21st of this month, all the members of the association would separately petition the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, the Citizens' Association, and the Municipal Council's He DeKui and others. (4) The motion to decide on the principles of the petition was resolved. A. Demand that the Municipal Council expedite the construction of public housing to avoid displacement of the slums. B. If the Municipal Council needs to properly build roads or the landowners formally build houses, relocation will be allowed. C. Slum representatives guarantee that the number of slums will not increase in the future. (5) The motion to investigate the number of slums and the population was resolved. It was decided that each representative would thoroughly investigate and report to the meeting for reference. (6) The motion to decide on the name of the association was resolved and named the Shanghai Slum United Association. (7) The motion that the slums are scattered in various districts, making contact difficult, and the association plans to establish branch offices in Pudong and Puxi separately to achieve effective communication was resolved and passed.

List of Preparatory Committee Members

Hu Yumen, Xu Yiqun, Tian Ruishan, Sun Weijin, Jiang Yibo, Wang Chengguang, Xu Xipeng, Liu Jinshan, Xu Jingqing, Deng Xiuzheng from Puxi slums; Wang Qitai, Sun Hongkui, Xu Xiyuan, Yin Yipu, Sun Xudan, Zhang Buyun, Yang Jinchen, Tang Anping, Gu Xuebo, Liu Xuezhuo, Wang Jiayu, Wang Daomeng, Guo Bingzhi, Jiang Shanchang, Ji Yunsheng, Jia Zilian, Zhang Ziying, Dong Maoxiang, Ye Shuting from Pudong slums; and 29 others.

There has also been a major disaster in the United States this year, which will inevitably lead to a poor harvest, so the flour price is temporarily difficult to fall. Chaos in the Cotton Yarn Market

Yarn Factories Sell Stored Cotton and Voluntarily Suspend or Reduce Production

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the prices in the cotton yarn market have soared recently due to manipulation by speculators, especially for marked cotton, resulting in an abnormal situation of expensive cotton and cheap yarn. The reason for the rise is ostensibly the rise in US cotton prices, but in reality, it is because speculators, aware that domestic yarn factories will lack a month's worth of raw materials when the old cotton runs out and the new cotton has not yet arrived, have bought in bulk in anticipation of making a fortune later, which has led to the increasingly rampant cotton price rise. However, according to a Shen Shi News Agency reporter's inquiry to the yarn factories, most yarn factories are finding it very difficult to maintain operations due to the expensive cotton and cheap yarn. It is also summer, and actual sales are sluggish. Therefore, recently, the factories have instead sold their stored cotton and voluntarily suspended or reduced production. On closer inspection, Shanghai has ample stored cotton. If the factories suspend or reduce production, there should be no shortage of cotton for use this year. Moreover, my country's cotton production will increase this year, which is certain. New cotton will be available in mid-July of the lunar calendar. Therefore, the recent rise in marked cotton is undoubtedly the result of manipulation by speculators.

Recent Status of the Surveying Work of the Yangtze River Channel

The Yangtze River channel from the north mouth to the Haizhou section is being surveyed by the Hydrographic Office of the Navy Department. The silt and reefs in this section of the channel are densely packed, and the shipping industry is afraid of it. The central and local authorities, in view of this, believe that the surveying of this section of the channel is necessary to develop the coastal area of this section. The Hydrographic Office specifically sent technical personnel to survey in sections, which has been going on for more than a year. Because the area is sparsely populated, the work is very difficult. It is estimated that it will take three years to complete all the work. At present, the coastline survey has been extended north to Rugao. After two months, it can advance to Haizhou. After the coastline survey is completed, the second step is to survey the waterway. At that time, surveying ships will be sent to carry out the survey in sections, and a refined blueprint will be produced, indicating the sections of reefs and silt, and signs will be set up on the surface of the reefs and silt to benefit the shipping industry.

Hydrographic Office Dispatches Warships to Sound the Mouth of the Yellow River

The Hydrographic Office, considering the water flow at the mouth of the Yellow River to be relatively slow, with sand and mud accumulating here, increasing day by day, and causing severe silting, which not only hinders navigation but also obstructs water flow, potentially leading to flooding, dispatched the Ganlu and Cheng Sheng survey ships some days ago to the mouth of the Yellow River to sound the silting situation. After the sounding work is completed, the second step will be to carry out dredging work.

Jiren Funeral Assistance Society Executes New By-Laws to Aid with Coffin Materials

Since its reorganization and membership drive, the Shanghai Jiren Funeral Assistance Society has successfully recruited 500 members for the "Ren" (Benevolence) group and declared its establishment. It is currently dispatching personnel to deliver material requisition reports to members household by household, and it is scheduled to begin executing its new by-laws to aid with coffin materials starting August 1st. It is also continuing to recruit members for the second group (i.e., the "Yi" [Righteousness] group), and the number of people voluntarily signing up remains enthusiastic. Yesterday (the 19th) at 1:00 PM, Mr. Shao Ruxin convened a meeting of all staff at the head office to decide on four action plans to be followed respectively: (1) The material production yard will immediately begin processing basic materials for distribution. (2) Investigators should pay attention to the length of the corpse during investigations, note it on the material requisition certificate, and issue materials based on the certificate to avoid bending the corpse. (3) The Society's material assistance completely avoids the form of charity. Therefore, employees should understand that the coffin is painted with gold "Shou" (Longevity) characters in seal script and has copper rings. They should not be arrogant, speak harshly, or urge the family of the deceased, but should allow the family to view the body calmly and express their grief. (4) The fixed cost of coffin material is set at 20 yuan per set, plus 2 yuan for lime and charcoal ash, and 3 yuan for carrying fees regardless of distance, totaling 25 yuan. Therefore, each member who assists with one coffin only needs to contribute 5 cents per share, 500 shares totaling 25 yuan, without costing the bereaved family a single penny. All employees are not allowed to privately solicit carrying fees or transportation costs to uphold morality. If verified, they will be severely punished. The Society will never solicit donations from the outside world.
