Economic Special

The North China Textile Industry Under Japanese Control

— Sen Yu

Recently, news about the decline of China's cotton textile industry has been continuously reported. According to last month's (June) statistics, the total number of yarn spindles in Chinese-owned mills nationwide is more than 2.7 million, with over 140,000 thread spindles, and more than 20,000 looms. However, 31.5% of the yarn spindles are idle, and among the 68.5% that are operating, 12.4% have reduced production, and 10% are about to reduce production. As for thread spindles and looms, a significant number are also idle. This situation is much worse than last year, which was already the worst year.

However, while Chinese-owned factories are closing down, selling off assets, and reducing production, Japanese-owned mills operating in China are continuously buying up factories, adding new ones, increasing spindles, and expanding production, achieving astonishing growth. Considering only yarn spindles for now, it is reported that they have reached a massive number of over 2.45 million, an increase of more than 500,000 compared to last year's 1.94 million, and the planned increases are not even included in this number.

Although Japanese capital has not abandoned Shanghai and Wuhan, it is evident that their focus has shifted to North China. This is closely related to the development of abnormal political power. Fundamentally, it is also part of the so-called "economic cooperation" invasion policy!

The active shift of Japanese mills towards North China began last year. In that year, Japanese merchants established three new factories in China, all concentrated in the Qingdao area. These include:

Earlier this year, Toyota Automatic Loom Works of Japan invested in the only Chinese-owned mill in Qingdao, Huaxin Yarn Factory, under a disguised form. Although nominally for replacing old machines with new ones, in reality, it is no different from the Chinese factory surrendering to Japanese capital. Therefore, the textile industry in Qingdao can be said to be entirely in the hands of Japanese merchants.

Moreover, this year, Japanese merchants have placed even greater emphasis on Tianjin, as it is a major industrial and commercial area in China, making business operations much more convenient. At the same time, Tianjin is under the jurisdiction of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council and is adjacent to the puppet autonomous region of Eastern Hebei, placing it directly and indirectly under Japanese political influence. This allows them to connect economic aggression and political aggression on the same line. They are not only focused on North China, but also intend to make Tianjin the center for monopolizing the yarn market throughout China.

Japanese mills are entering and expanding in Tianjin through the following three methods: (1) buying up Chinese factories, (2) expanding existing factories, and (3) adding new factories. Under the strategy of buying up Chinese factories, the existing factories in Tianjin have successively fallen into the hands of Japanese capital. The current situation of the local Chinese-owned yarn factories is briefly described below:

Yuyuan: This is the largest yarn factory in Tianjin, established in April of the seventh year of the Republic of China (1918), with a capital of 5.6 million yuan. Internally, it is divided into the first, second, and third yarn factories and a weaving factory, with a total of 71,360 yarn spindles, 9,760 thread spindles, 1,000 looms, and 3,000 workers. Due to poor business performance in recent years, it has accumulated debts, and announced a shutdown on January 11th last year. As of last year, it owed a total of 5.17 million yuan in secured debt to Chinese and Japanese consortiums, of which the loan from Okura & Co. of Japan amounted to more than 3.3 million Japanese yen, accounting for more than 60%. In addition, 3 million shares have also flowed into Japanese hands. Due to Okura & Co.'s urgent demand for repayment and the machinations of Japanese shareholders, it had no choice but to liquidate and sell. Japanese merchants had long intended to swallow this factory. Lending money and acquiring shares were merely tactics in the process of annexation. After a long period of preparation, Yuyuan Yarn Factory was officially acquired by Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd. of Japan in May of this year. It is currently actively renovating its machinery and equipment, with operations scheduled to start in September. After resuming operations, it plans to expand to 150,000 spindles. In addition to spinning fine yarn, it will also engage in weaving cotton cloth. As for the name, it will likely be changed to Gongda No. 6 Factory. From then on, the largest yarn factory in Tianjin has fallen into the hands of Japanese capital, and an important fighter in the national industry has lost its final fate!

Beiyang: With a capital of 3.9 million yuan, it has a total of 26,752 yarn spindles, 2,128 thread spindles, and more than 1,300 workers, with a daily output of more than 60 bales. Due to excessive losses, it temporarily shut down in June of last year. Subsequently, it increased its capital by 200,000 yuan, reorganized, and resumed operations, but recently it was unable to struggle and declared bankruptcy again. Last month (June), the factory was also acquired by Japanese capital, and the successor is Shanghai Yufeng Yarn Factory. (Editor's note: The Tianjin telegram of this newspaper on the 17th stated that only Hengyuan and Beiyang No. 3 factories are left under the management of Chinese.)

Baocheng: With a capital of 3 million yuan, it has a total of 27,028 yarn spindles, 2,520 thread spindles, and 1,200 workers, with a daily output of 53 bales. The factory's products were originally mostly sold to the Northeast. Since the Northeast was lost, the market was cut off, resulting in increasing losses and making it impossible to continue operations. On July 17th, it was auctioned off by the creditor bank group and was formally acquired by Okura Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd. of Yuda Yarn Factory for a price of 1.375 million yuan, officially falling under Japanese ownership.

Huaxin: With a capital of over 2.42 million yuan, it has a total of 27,072 yarn spindles and 1,000 workers. The factory's machinery and hygiene facilities are among the best of all factories. Unfortunately, due to the decline in business, internal shareholders have recently had deep disagreements. According to the Shen Bao on the 16th of this month, it is showing signs of being sold off like Yuyuan, Beiyang, and Baocheng. At the same time, the Japanese side is watching intently. It is reported that the Dai-Nippon Spinning Co., Ltd. is also planning to take over. In the near future, this Huaxin Yarn Factory will probably be unreliable as well.

Hengyuan: With a capital of 4 million yuan, it originally had 35,440 yarn spindles, 2,540 thread spindles, and 310 looms. Due to business losses, it had debts of more than one million yuan and declared bankruptcy in 1934. At that time, it was rumored that the Japanese Oriental Development Company would take over, but fortunately, that did not become a reality. It is now managed by the Chengfu Trust Company, jointly formed by the China, Central, Jin, and Cheng Salt Industries Banks. They plan to add more than 20,000 yarn spindles and 400 looms, with a planned daily output of more than 100 bales of yarn and 1,400 bolts of cloth. However, we still cannot be fully optimistic about its future. Under the heavy pressure from the Japanese side, it is very difficult to guarantee that it will not follow the path of the aforementioned factories.

Dasheng: Established in 1932, it initially only twisted thread. It only started spinning yarn last year. With a capital of 200,000 yuan, it has a total of 5,000 yarn spindles and 400 workers, with a monthly output of about 300 bales of yarn. Because the factory is small, many people do not pay attention to it. However, due to its recent establishment, all the machines used are new, and the production efficiency is high, and the production cost is relatively low, so it seems to have the hope of development. However, the Japanese side probably won't show much mercy to this rising star. In such an abnormal situation in North China, we still have to harbor infinite worries.

Looking at the above six yarn factories, Dasheng is newly established, and the only remaining old factory is Hengyuan, which is operated by a consortium. Yuyuan, Beiyang (?), and Baocheng have been acquired by Japanese capital, and Huaxin is also in danger. If we include Yuda (with a capital of 3 million yuan, 35,712 yarn spindles, and 1,500 thread spindles), which is already in the hands of Japanese merchants, the vast majority of the power of the Tianjin textile industry is actually held by the Japanese side. Here, we can make another simple comparison:

According to the above table, the Japanese side will account for:

81.2% of the capital of Tianjin's yarn factories, while the Chinese side will account for 18.8%. The Japanese side will account for 82.3% of the yarn spindles, while the Chinese side will account for 17.7%. The Japanese side will account for 73.7% of the thread spindles, while the Chinese side will account for 26.3%. These proportions are already alarming enough, but it doesn't stop there. Japanese merchants are also actively expanding the above-mentioned factories. Yuda Yarn Factory, with the support of Dai-Nippon Spinning Co., Ltd., plans to expand to 50,000 spindles. Yuyuan Yarn Factory, with the support of Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd., plans to expand to 150,000 spindles. In addition, Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd. is also building a Yufeng branch factory in Tianjin, with a planned 100,000 yarn spindles. Toyo Spinning Co., Ltd. has recently held a groundbreaking ceremony for a new yarn factory, which can be completed by the end of this year, with 150,000 yarn spindles in the future. At the same time, Dai-Nippon Spinning Co., Ltd., Kanebo Spinning Co., Ltd., and Toyo Spinning Co., Ltd. plan to adopt a production cooperation system to jointly build a large factory that can accommodate 150,000 yarn spindles. Also, there is news that Toyo Spinning Co., Ltd., Osaka Spinning Co., Ltd., and Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd. are also jointly establishing a new factory. The first step is to install 50,000 yarn spindles, and the second step is to complete 100,000 yarn spindles next year. It is reported that Japanese merchants have unanimously decided to add at least 600,000 yarn spindles in Tianjin. Then, adding the 200,000 or so spindles in the above table, Tianjin alone will reach a massive 800,000 spindles. The Japanese ambition to control the North China textile market can be said to have been completely achieved.

In addition to Qingdao and Tianjin, it is naturally very difficult for Chinese-owned yarn factories in North China to gain a foothold elsewhere. For example, the Tangshan branch of Huaxin, with 28,000 yarn spindles, is virtually on its last legs under the various devastation and double taxation burdens of the puppet organization in Eastern Hebei. As for the other factories in Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi, they are also struggling under severe oppression and are in imminent danger. And it's not just North China that's like this, the entire domestic textile industry is facing a total collapse. In addition, smuggling is rampant, and large quantities of cotton cloth flood into various regions, making the livelihood of the weaving industry even more fatally devastated.

Furthermore, the Japanese side is using all means to monopolize raw cotton. Under the slogan of "Industrial Japan, Agricultural China," North China's cotton production will be completely plundered. The cotton field area in Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi provinces accounts for 33% of the total cotton field area in the country, and the production volume accounts for 35% of the total production volume in the country, with an average annual output of about 5 million dan. Furthermore, under the entire invasion program of the Japanese government and the South Manchuria Railway Company, and the "North China Cotton Five-Year Plan" centered on Kanegafuchi Spinning Co., Ltd. and Toyo Spinning Co., Ltd., they plan to more actively expand cotton fields in North China, improve seeds, first focusing on Eastern Hebei and Eastern Shandong, then Shanxi, and even extending to Shaanxi and Henan provinces. They are determined to make North China an unlimited supply base of raw cotton for the Japanese textile industry, and the farmers of North China will be cotton-planting slaves for life, so that the cotton used by Japanese factories will no longer depend on imports from the United States, India, and Egypt.

Therefore, not only the production and sales of yarn and cloth are monopolized by the Japanese side, but also the supply of raw cotton is unreasonably controlled. From now on, everything in the cotton textile industry will be manipulated by Japanese capital, and China's only national industry will face the danger of premature death!

According to Rong Zongjing, due to the impact of the dumping of products from Japanese mills, Chinese merchants are currently losing 70-80 cents per bale of yarn produced and 30 yuan per piece of cloth. If timely rescue measures are not taken, in the future, it may not even be possible to lose money! So, how to save the industry? We have also heard that the government is providing relief and the banking sector is providing assistance, but so far, these are still castles in the air. According to the Zhonghua Daily on the 10th of this month, a reporter asked Rong Zongjing about the yarn factories' petition to the Ministry of Industry for assistance, and Rong's reply was: "This has been chanted for three years, but nothing has been done in reality!" What a painful sigh! In addition, in early May, we saw the leaders of the Bank of China jointly form the Textile Industry Management Association to rescue the North China textile industry, and held a meeting in Zhengzhou to discuss the methods for purchasing cotton, spinning yarn, and selling prices. At that time, it seemed to show a glimmer of dawn for the North China textile industry. However, more than two months have passed, and we have not heard of any specific follow-up!

Originally, the decline of China's cotton textile industry is definitely not a simple issue of so-called "market depression." It is the inevitable result of political and economic aggression by certain parties. Therefore, even if the above-mentioned "rescue" is done well, it will only be a temporary fix and not a thorough solution. We must remember the gunpowder smell contained in "economic cooperation" and "industrial ×× agricultural China." How to get China out of the shackles of a colony or semi-colony is our fundamental way out!

The Smuggling Problem

— Wang Haifan

The issue of smuggling in our country has existed for a long time. Anyone who understands the commercial situation in Shanghai and has a certain understanding of its inner workings knows that there are so-called "white goods" and "red goods" in rayon and cigarette paper. These terms are euphemisms for official goods and smuggled goods. Although the annual loss of customs duties cannot be statistically determined, it is probably considerable. However, it is reported that there are also considerable organizations among these people, with tea parties and market prices. For smuggled goods from certain sources, some only send the goods to the port, some guarantee landing, and some act as agents for transshipment, guaranteeing all risks and sending them to the sales venues of these people. All of these involve collaboration between Chinese traitors and Japanese ruffians, relying on the protection of foreign forces to cover the ears and eyes of customs officials. Once the smuggled goods land and reach the sales agencies, there is no risk of being caught, even when transshipped inland. The "passes" for paying taxes can be substituted and used fraudulently, so that "white goods" are no different from "red goods." This is a general overview of smuggling in the past. As for whether the facts are really like this, it is certainly not something that outsiders can know. And now with the rampant smuggling in North China, penetrating deep into the interior, some believe that it is caused by excessive customs duties. Such as Ross's remarks upon returning home, advocating for reducing tax rates, but what they do not know is that our country's tax rates, on the whole, are still lower than those of countries like England, America, Germany, France, and Japan. We know that a country's import tariffs, without violating the most-favored-nation clause, have the right to be freely determined. Even if the tax rate is high, Japanese merchants should abide by the provisions of the treaty and comply with China's customs regulations. They cannot use this as an excuse to implement smuggling and tax evasion, acting recklessly without restraint. Moreover, according to recent customs investigations, smuggled goods are not limited to expensive and heavily taxed items such as rayon. Various fruits and seafood are also frequently smuggled. If that is the case, then the promotion of smuggling is definitely not due to excessive tax rates.

So, where does the main cause lie? First, it is due to the urgent need for Japanese goods to find a way out. Since the occupation of the four northeastern provinces, industry has flourished. Last year, due to the expansion of occupied territories and the special opportunity of the Italo-Ethiopian War, foreign trade achieved a new record. This year, since January, the total amount of import surplus in the first quarter reached more than 215 million yuan, an increase of more than 53 million yuan compared to the same period last year. However, exports have ultimately failed to increase in tandem. Proportionally, the export amount increased by 4% compared to the same period last year, while the import amount increased by 9% compared to the same period last year. Under this situation, the Japanese had no choice but to urgently seek market expansion. However, looking around, countries are panicking all day long, all regarding 1936 as an extraordinary period, loudly advocating self-sufficiency policies, and gradually moving towards wartime controlled economies. Free trade is not easy to achieve today. And how can the dream of the Far East Economic Bloc be realized? Therefore, in order to achieve its goals, it does not hesitate to allow and tolerate smuggling.

Secondly, disrupting finance is originally one of the policies of the aggressor. The smuggling problem is almost as the London Times said on May 18th, "This matter is not just a local action by Japanese soldiers..." This is evidenced by the seizure of privately transported silver coins in North China from January to May of last year. At this time, maritime smuggling had not yet expanded. Why did the Japanese side make a request that our country's customs anti-smuggling ships could not perform their duties in the war zone? Why were the anti-smuggling personnel along the Great Wall at the same time disarmed? Allowing illegal elements to become increasingly rampant. Moreover, after our side repeatedly requested assistance, why did they shirk responsibility and simply ignore it? Subsequently, our country's Ministry of Foreign Affairs lodged a serious protest, but why has there been no result to this day? Furthermore, countries like England and America, based on their own interests, have all formally questioned the Japanese government, but why have they not been able to get to the bottom of it? From this perspective, the situation is obvious. Although they want to destroy our finances and shake our markets, their long-term plans are not new. Before and after our country implemented legal tender last year, they first thought of using huge amounts of paper money to create a terrifying run on the banks. Later, Japanese merchants in Shanghai proposed using Japanese currency in the Chinese market to carry out their conspiracy of disruption. Although the matter has not been put into practice, if their plan had succeeded, the disaster would have been even greater than smuggling. Moreover, today's smuggling is no longer comparable to the previous petty theft and tax evasion. On the sea, ships follow each other, fully loaded. On land, they drive out guests and load goods, obstructing railway traffic. Those in charge of these activities have large-scale trade associations and other ruffian organizations. Without a background, how could they be so rampant?

Contemporary scholars discussing the prevention of smuggling and tax evasion advocate for encouraging informants and strictly cracking down on smuggling. However, the government's current punitive regulations for tax evasion state that those evading more than one thousand yuan must face life imprisonment, and in severe cases, the death penalty. The prohibitions are not insignificant. For reward methods, for anyone who provides information and leads to an arrest and punishment, there is a reward of 50%. The incentives are not ungenerous. However, smuggled goods continue to pour in, rampaging through the market, with a strong and uncurbed momentum. Anti-smuggling efforts encounter obstruction, leading to assault and insult, which is heard every day. Today, the situation has become increasingly deteriorated. As a result, national tax revenues are shrinking day by day, and industry and commerce are in imminent danger. What measures do we have to deal with this serious problem? Encouraging informants and strictly cracking down on smuggling, in today's environment, can they be effective? As for seeking Japanese understanding and assistance, it is impossible. As for whether the tax rate should be revised, we already know that it is definitely not the reason for smuggling. Sir Ross's words are well-intentioned, but our government should have its own opinions. We fear that if we follow his words, smuggling will not stop, and the country's losses will be even greater. For the current plan, in the active aspect, other than using strength to adjust the special status of North China in order to achieve a thorough success, there is no other good strategy. In the passive aspect, merchants should feel the pain personally, strictly strengthen their own organizations, report smuggled goods, and sanction Chinese traitors, so that once the way out for smuggled goods is cut off, the way in will naturally be blocked. The former is initiated by the government, with the people as the backing. The latter is initiated by the people, with the government as the backing. If this is the case, it may be possible to achieve effectiveness in the slightest chance. If we continue to act perfunctorily and do not devise effective countermeasures, simply seeking to open up new sources of revenue due to insufficient tax revenue, then people will covet private gain, and there will be no end to it. In that case, the disasters that follow may be worse than floods and wild beasts.

Deliberations on Domestic Product Inspection

— Xin Zhi

—Regarding the issue of "People's Automatic Handling"—

In the past, we have had many painful experiences, where originally well-intentioned improvement endeavors often yielded the opposite results. The recent implementation of domestic product inspection by the Ministry of Industry is at such a crossroads.

The original intention of domestic product inspection is not only a type of agricultural improvement endeavor, but also a matter of utmost urgency today. The main focus of domestic product inspection is place-of-origin inspection. In China today, where industry is not yet highly developed and agriculture still occupies an important position in the national economy, the so-called domestic products are naturally mainly agricultural products. Therefore, domestic product inspection, in a narrow sense, can also be called place-of-origin inspection of agricultural products. The reasons for agricultural products to undergo place-of-origin inspection are very clear: First, the quality of various agricultural products in China today is too mixed, and inspection can passively promote improvement in production; second, guaranteeing excellent quality and identifying quality grades helps with the conduct of sales; third, cracking down on the bad habits of adulteration and counterfeiting enhances the reputation of products. The agricultural production relations in China today are extremely complex. The reasonable implementation of domestic product inspection, in addition to striving to improve the quality of agricultural products, must not only consider the interests of merchants and the people, but also the interests of farmers.

China has had many years of history in the inspection administration of import and export commodities, and domestic product inspection, mainly for domestic sales, is a new initiative. At the beginning of its inception, it is inevitable to refer to the effectiveness of implementation in some advanced countries.

Let us first look at the situation in Japan. The background of Japan's inspection administration: the national territory is not large, and the institutions of various sectors of society are not only organized but also unified. Under such favorable conditions, it seems that inspection work is easy to promote and can be "automatically handled by the people"? However, Japan's inspection administration has also taken great pains.

Japan's inspection work is divided into two types: one is the inspection of industrial products, and the other is the inspection of agricultural products. The inspection of industrial products can be said to be "automatically handled by the people," but it has also undergone important reforms. Japan's industrial product inspection agencies are all "industrial associations" of the respective industries. If we regard these industrial associations as exactly the same in nature as our country's trade associations, then that is completely wrong. It can only be said that they are equivalent to our country's current trade associations, which in Japan are "industry associations." Because the Japanese have strong organizational skills, in some situations, they are much more organized and powerful than our country's current trade associations. Since the global economic panic occurred after 1929 and trade wars intensified among countries, the Japanese government knew that to cope with the current economic war, it was necessary to improve the quality of Japanese goods and reduce costs at the same time. The method used to achieve this goal was the so-called "people's autonomous control." The most suitable agency to implement this "autonomous control" seems to be the industry association. However, the Japanese government still considered the strength of the industry associations to be insufficient and separately promulgated the Industrial Association Law, so that various industries automatically organized industrial associations to carry out: (1) active mutual assistance in production, (2) passive inspection and control (such as prices) two major tasks.

But this is only the situation in the industrial sector, the agricultural sector is completely different. Japan's so-called "autonomous control" (including automatic inspection) is limited to commodity producers themselves, so only industrial products are possible. The direct producers of agricultural products are scattered small farmers (Japan still maintains fragmented small-scale farming). These farmers are still culturally very backward, and it is impossible for them to automatically inspect their own agricultural products. Therefore, the inspection of agricultural products is purely the work of the government.

Agricultural inspection in Japan is part of the work of local governments. Because agricultural production is scattered throughout the country and the situation in each place is different, it is necessary to handle them separately according to the specific circumstances. Therefore, agricultural inspection in Japan varies from prefecture to prefecture, and the types of inspections also differ. People's organizations such as local agricultural associations and "inspection associations" only stand in a supplementary position (for details, see the Japan Agricultural Product Inspection Survey Report published by the Upper Commodity Inspection Bureau).

The inspection of agricultural products in the United States is also the same, all handled by the government. (Same as above, published in the International Trade Guide, Volume 6, Number 9)

After looking at these references, let's look at China's agricultural inspection methods.

At the second meeting on April 24 of this year (1936), the Domestic Product Inspection Committee of the Ministry of Industry resolved on six "Basic Principles of the Domestic Product Inspection System":

1. Start with cracking down on adulteration and counterfeiting, with the aim of identifying grades.

2. First promoted by the government, with the hope that it will gradually be handled automatically by the people, under the supervision and guidance of the government, but the inspection methods and grading standards must be submitted to the Ministry (Ministry of Industry) for approval, and the inspectors must be recognized by the competent inspection agency of the Ministry.

3. Domestic sales inspection of domestic products should start from collection and distribution markets or places of origin.

4. The government will not charge handling fees for domestic sales inspection of domestic products.

5. Samples taken for domestic sales inspection of domestic products will be returned after inspection.

6. Inspection procedures should be simplified as much as possible, and strict time limits for inspection should be set to facilitate commercial transportation.

In terms of these six principles, it cannot be said that considerations are not comprehensive. However, in terms of the second principle, if strict regulations are not given, it is difficult to avoid being the main reason for leading domestic product inspection down a wrong path. The provision in the budget allocation of the resolution: "Those who are self-operated by merchant groups shall raise funds for handling by the respective groups themselves," further leads inspection into a wrong path. Although the detailed rules for the implementation of various domestic product inspections are separately stipulated, these six principles must be generally applicable.

First of all, what we need to study is: What kind of "people" are the so-called people who automatically handle it? According to the words "automatically," it is naturally the operators of various industries, such as the inspection of light bulbs by light bulb manufacturers, and the inspection of cotton cloth by cotton cloth manufacturers. The nature that can be applied to this is naturally limited to the industrial product sector. If agricultural products are also "automatically handled by the people," then only the farmers themselves who are direct producers are qualified.

Let's start with industrial products first. To achieve the goal of people's automatic inspection, the people must first have complete, close-knit, and powerful organizations, and these organizations must be purely automatic by the operators. Such an organization that is sufficient to bear this responsibility does not exist today. The most important organizations of industrialists and merchants in China today are the chambers of commerce and trade associations in various places. The members contained in the chamber of commerce are extremely complex. Only in the past when industry was underdeveloped, the social classes were still three categories: direct producer farmers, seller merchants, and governing government. Only at that time was the chamber of commerce the only people's organization. Now, the interests of the producer industrialists and the purely selling merchants are different, and the work is even more divergent. As seen in Mr. Hu Xiyuan's recent request for the promulgation of the Industrial Association Law, this is a manifestation of this fact. Furthermore, in terms of the internal situation of existing chambers of commerce, most cannot be said to be powerful, nor can they be said to be well-organized, resulting in things such as bribery, embezzlement, and flight of executive members. In addition, fundamentally, the chamber of commerce does not see "operators," so there is no "automatic handling" to speak of.

The trade association is more suitable for the condition of being an organization of operators. However, the trade associations in China today cannot bear this responsibility either: First, in many trade industries today, most are not organizations of industrial producers, but organizations of sales merchants. They naturally cannot talk about "automatic handling." If they can "automatically handle it," then what is "passively" handled is not their own products, but other people's. The result is that they overstep their authority to interfere with others, and the function of "automatic" is completely lost. Second, even if there are some organizations of industrial producers, these trade associations still cannot get rid of the remnants of the past industrial guilds, or are even simply something like a club. For example, recently, when smuggling became rampant, all parties attached importance to the trade association playing a role. As a result, Mr. Ma Yinchu and others came to the conclusion of reorganizing and strengthening the trade association.

Therefore, in terms of industrial products, automatic inspection by the people is possible, but there must first be an organization that can bear this responsibility, and the government can absolutely control this organization. Before Japan announced the Industrial Association, the strength and organization of all industry associations were probably much higher than those existing in China, but the Japanese government thought it was not enough and re-promulgated the Industrial Association Law, giving the power of automatic inspection of industrial products to the industrial associations of various industries.

We know that the problem of domestic product inspection in China does not lie in industrial products, but in agricultural products. The main body of domestic product inspection is actually only agricultural product inspection. If agricultural product inspection is to apply the second of the "basic principles," then only the farmers themselves, who are direct producers, are qualified. But we clearly know that the scattered individual small farmers themselves will not have the strength to "automatically handle" it. If they can automatically handle it, then in the place of origin, there must be local tyrants and evil gentry, under the guise of farmers, establishing groups and contracting inspections. In the "collection and distribution center," there must be commercial capitalists, presuming to be "operators," "automatically" inspecting for farmers. In this way, the government originally intended to avoid establishing more agencies, but as a result, the gentry and merchants have established more agencies for the government. Not only can this not achieve the government's original intention, but the severity of the disaster is unimaginable. Because anyone can use the second "basic principle" as an excuse to organize groups as much as possible to inspect for farmers, and can use the proposal of "raising funds on their own" as a talisman to increase the exploitation of farmers.

This is not alarmist. Soon after the resolution of the Domestic Product Inspection Committee was announced, the wealthy gentry and market hooligans had already risen up in droves, organizing groups to "help" the government.

Agricultural inspection handled by the people has no precedents to follow in various countries. In terms of China's actual situation, malpractices will inevitably arise. Why? As mentioned earlier, since farmers cannot "automatically" handle it, and merchants handle it, the effect of "automatic" by the operators has already been lost. Moreover, in terms of the actual situation in Chinese rural areas, merchants often stand in a position contrary to the interests of farmers. Most of the adulteration and fraud in various agricultural products are also done by intermediate selling merchants. If merchants who are sellers inspect agricultural products, no matter how strong the government's supervision is, it will be of no benefit to farmers.

We believe that "people's automatic handling" of agricultural product inspection is not yet the time! If the government is determined to make the inspection work be done by the people automatically, then not only must organizational work be done in advance, but the government's control power must also be specially strengthened. Otherwise, if the power of inspection falls into the hands of rural wealthy gentry and market hooligans, then it will inevitably be "the original intention was a very good improvement undertaking, but the results obtained are often the opposite."

Wheat Inspection Methods

— Xi

Wheat is a major staple food of our people. In recent years, due to frequent disasters and the increase in population, it has become insufficient. The amount of foreign wheat imported last year almost ranked first among imports. In this intersection of people's livelihood and economic distress, how to increase production to enrich the domestic food supply, how to diligently implement controls to balance the surpluses and deficits of food in various places. And the implementation of inspection undertakings, in a passive aspect, can prevent adulteration and counterfeiting and reduce losses; in an active aspect, can improve quality and facilitate transportation, sales and storage. It can directly increase the interests of producers, sellers and consumers, and indirectly can help the rural areas. Revitalize and develop various industries to stabilize the national life. Therefore, various countries regard food inspection as an important government affair, and there is a good reason for this.

The importance of wheat inspection has been described earlier. However, this kind of undertaking is still a new initiative in our country. What kind of policy should be adopted, and what should be the steps? This is indeed a prerequisite for the implementation of inspection. In order to facilitate promotion and achieve great results, it is especially important to consider carefully. Now, after summing up the opinions of all parties. All believe that the steps of wheat inspection should start with cracking down on the mixing of water and adulteration, followed by grade, and then quality. I do not know that in terms of China's actual situation, the crackdown on wheat should start with simple grading.

The purpose of inspection undertakings is (1) to improve the grade of products, (2) to guarantee and unify the quality and quantity of products, (3) to improve the method of buying and selling, (4) to rationalize storage or preservation. It is a comprehensive body of grain improvement facilities, inspection facilities and treatment improvement facilities. Each facility has an inseparable and rapid lock relationship, and must be harmonized with each other to exert its function. And just to improve the grade of products, it can be divided into three types: quality improvement, drying improvement, and preparation improvement, which are also related. At present, various facilities in our country are not perfect. Large-scale preparation and drying equipment still need to be promoted and promoted. Farmers and merchants also lack a considerable understanding of inspection policies and need publicity. In this transition period, if strict crackdown regulations are to be established and enforced, there will inevitably be many obstacles in fact, which goes without saying. For example, if a large batch of wheat is inspected as unqualified during transportation, at this time it is not allowed to be bought and sold, and there is no preparation and drying equipment to make it re-improve the product, how will it be dealt with? If you want to implement according to the regulations, it is inevitably too harsh. If you change the handling, you violate the original intention. Therefore, it is not easy to implement the crackdown for a while, and you should seek another way. Before implementing the crackdown, you can adopt a laissez-faire policy and conduct simple grading inspections in the wheat collection and distribution market. The main purpose of this inspection is to only grade without cracking down. It can avoid the difficulties caused by the crackdown methods, and graded wheat can be priced according to grade in the market trade, which still implies the intention of rewarding the superior and depreciating the inferior. Farmers and merchants know that wheat that has undergone grading inspection can get a considerable price, and they can gradually be influenced and understand the need for inspection. Then, when strict crackdown regulations are formulated and promoted, various difficulties can be solved easily. This is why cracking down on the mixing of water and adulteration of wheat should start with simple grading.

Summer in West Lake

— (Yao Mingran)

Everyone knows the beauty of the mountains and waters of West Lake. And the summer West Lake is an even more worthy place to sing praises! From Su Dongpo's poem about West Lake in June: "After all, West Lake in the sixth month is different from the scenery of the four seasons; the lotus leaves connecting to the sky are infinitely green, and the lotus flowers reflecting the sun are especially red"! Extraordinary Period—Summer

— Hua Ling

Summer is the most dangerous season of the year, because in summer, the activity of all terrible germs is often the highest of the year. Recently, people like to say an "extraordinary period" for everything. From a sanitary point of view, "summer" should also be considered an extraordinary period of the year.

During extraordinary periods, everyone is careful about air defense. In our summer life, I feel that "air defense issues" are also very important. Our air enemy is the fly. Each fly is like an airplane that releases poison gas, spreading cholera germs, typhoid germs, dysentery germs, etc., and causing people to die. The most effective method for enemy aircraft is to shoot down one when it comes, and shoot down two when two come. For flies, naturally, kill one when it comes, and kill two when two come. The passive method is naturally to imitate the method of air defense, covering the food with a gauze cover so that the flies cannot come into contact with the food. But the fundamental way, then I think, should be "national defense first" as a motto, to make the room clean, and flies avoid it far away. During extraordinary periods, in addition to air defense, the drinking water problem is also very important, because in the tense atmosphere, there is always a danger of enemies placing poison in the waterways. In this extraordinary period of our year, even if you drink a sip of plain water, you always have to drink it boiled to avoid the danger of enemy germs. The water in the inland rivers cannot be drunk without boiling it. Even the tap water in the city, which looks very clean, is questionable whether it is bacteria-free after passing through long water pipes. Even if the tap water is 100% clean, it is difficult to guarantee that the bacteria attached to the drinking utensils will not invade the human body with it once it is released. So even if it is tap water, it is safe to drink it boiled to avoid poisoning. Mosquitoes, as everyone knows, are the medium for transmitting infectious germs. Although they are not as terrible as flies that spread germs, their sneaky expression is quite similar to the needle attack that was all the rage in Sichuan some time ago. It is also a major enemy in the extraordinary period, and it is urgent to find a way to eliminate it. In addition, things like bedbugs and cockroaches are somewhat like spies who are disrupting the rear. If they are not strictly searched and arrested, it may also affect the entire situation.

Summer Morning

— Zhou Xian

When my classmates write about summer, they always like to write about summer nights. Indeed, in the summer night, it is true that there are many mysterious and heavy atmospheres, which are worthy of the infatuation of homeless wanderers, and worthy of the praise, or sigh, curse, or satire of optimistic, or pessimistic poets, artists, painters, and other emotional people. But I feel that there is a special taste in the summer morning.

Although all the wine houses and dance halls have turned off the charming red lights at two o'clock the night before, when the sun has just climbed up from the horizon with a shining top, the 1936-style streamlined cars, when entering the city from the suburbs, are all carrying pairs of men and women, young gentlemen, and modern girls. The young gentlemen's hair has escaped the control of Tai Liang Si Taikang, and it is messily covering their foreheads. The modern girls have also faded the rouge on their cheeks and the lipstick on their lips. The dullness in their eyes shows the fatigue of the whole night, yearning for the joy of nightlife in the sea, suburbs, or parks, they have forgotten all the summer depression.

On the sidewalk, on the narrow and dirty sidewalk, people are lying like sleepers, arranged in rows. They are all seeking a life in the city of material civilization, but they have not enjoyed the blessings of modern material civilization. They curse the cruelty of urban life, but they do not have the courage to escape this city. They are oppressed by mosquitoes and bedbugs in the house and cannot get the rest to recover from the fatigue of the day. At the same time, they are steamed by the stagnant air in the house and feel difficulty in breathing. So they have to sit on the ground and seek a sweet dream life. But the ruthless dung truck, turning the heavy iron wheels, awakens the good dreams of some people, and the little smile on anyone's face is driven away. That's right, it's time for another day of hard work to begin.

But, outside of these two scenes, in another area of the same city, there are large, square, three-dimensional foreign houses, surrounded by flowers and trees. The golden sun kisses the green treetops, showing the grace and luxury of the summer morning. In the quiet air, on the lawn surrounded by wire mesh, the sound of a tennis ball occasionally comes out. Through the gaps in the wire mesh, a scene of a noble Westerner hitting a tennis ball is displayed. At the same time, on another lawn, several Chinese amahs are leading a group of Western children, playing and jumping. Although they also live in this city, their lives seem to be in another world.

Looking at the Melon Patch

— Jin Sulan

The wheels of time keep turning, and it's summer. The weather is unusually hot, and watermelons, that wonderful product for cooling off, are ripening one after another.

Chen Quanfu planted four acres of watermelon fields, a lush green expanse where watermelons of various sizes lie quietly under the dense foliage.

When the watermelons are almost ripe, they need careful protection. Chen Quanfu used several reed mats to build a low shed at the edge of the field, laying a tattered straw mat inside. He spends his entire day hiding in it, guarding the watermelons.

He carries a dry tobacco pipe and a sharp fish spear with him. When he is bored and lonely, he smokes a few pipes of dry tobacco, which is enough to break the silence and invigorate his spirit.

He is like a high monk in deep meditation, sitting cross-legged in the small shed, closing his eyes to rest. He seems to be asleep, but his hearing is still very sharp, fulfilling his duty. Occasionally, if he hears a dog barking or the footsteps of a passerby from the road, he wakes up as if shocked by electricity. He pokes his head out of the shed to look around. Seeing no movement and that his watermelons are safe and sound, he retreats back into the shed.

At night, he is deeply afraid that bad people will come to steal watermelons, so he dares not fall asleep all night. He perks up his spirit, watching the field with wide eyes and listening attentively. When he is so tired that he keeps yawning, he lights his dry tobacco pipe and smokes it desperately to refresh himself. He smokes with such force that the white copper pipe emits a creaking groan.

The field is quiet, and everything seems to be fast asleep. Small sheds, like mounds of earth, are scattered like stars. The guards are all on alert, so even if thieves are bold, they would not dare to use their tricks.

Suddenly, a rustling sound comes from the field, which is a hedgehog gnawing at the watermelon. Chen Quanfu hates these detestable creatures. He immediately grabs his fish spear and rushes out, but the vigilant hedgehog has already run far away.

Chen Quanfu feels extremely hot and stuffy in the shed, but he hopes that the weather will be hotter than 100 degrees, so that the price of watermelons will become increasingly expensive. Then he can earn a lot of money, enough for his family to live on for half a year.

Various Roses

— Yan Bokuang

On the hills, thorny roses are planted everywhere, blooming with delicate flowers. The rich, sweet fragrance is blown into people's nostrils by the gentle breeze. How delightful! Among flowers, roses are considered to have it all: "color, fragrance, and taste."

Rose flowers: Pick roses from the branches, dry them over charcoal fire, and store them in lime jars. When serving tea to guests, put two roses on top. The fragrance can stay in the mouth and cheeks. Roses have "color, fragrance, and taste." Everyone says so.

During the rose season, Suzhou candy stores sell very good rose jam. But when I was working in Suzhou, I asked a Suzhou person what food goes best with rose jam. According to him, it's best to eat it with white zongzi. The red and white colors complement each other, making it beautiful and delicious.

Rose flower wine is also very good. Rose dew is made by collecting roses, putting them in a distillation pot, and applying heat to turn them into flower dew. It's a wonderful drink to quench thirst in the hot summer.

Roses have many uses. After baking and drying them, they can be crushed into powder and mixed into various pastries, which are very popular.

Special Report

Municipal Swimming Pool

— Ya Fei

Summer is, as usual, a season for "mermaids" to be active. So these days, in every swimming pool, we can enjoy the acrobatics of those "mermaids" leaping and splashing in the waves. Especially those "beautiful mermaids," their beautiful curves and lively postures give us the temptation and courage to try.

Shanghai has no shortage of swimming pools. There are the Hongkou Swimming Pool and the Sports Garden Swimming Pool nearby. Further away, there is the Gaoqiao Seaside Swimming Beach. There are also several semi-public ones such as the YMCA and the Liangjiang Southeast East Asia. But since the opening of the Municipal Swimming Pool in the city center, swimming enthusiasts have had another paradise for fitness and cooling off in the summer.

Although I am not good at swimming, I still like it, so I often like to stroll around in several swimming pools. However, since the Municipal Swimming Pool was completed, I only went once during the National Games to visit Yang Xiuqiong, and I haven't had the chance to go again since then. Now that it is open, I naturally have to find a way to visit it.

On a day when the sun was burning like fire, I wanted to escape the sweltering heat of ninety-seven or ninety-eight degrees, so I took a streamlined motorcycle with Jun and climbed onto the smooth Qimei Road, speeding towards the city center. In less than twenty minutes, we got out of the car in a large open space. Looking up, we saw the majestic and magnificent swimming pool, with its two iron gates open, standing there smiling like a dignified gentleman, greeting us politely.

Jun went to the women's changing room to change, as usual, and I walked into the men's changing room on the right. When the two of us came out of the glass doors on both sides, there were already many male and female "mermaids" in and around the swimming pool who were there before us.

In the rectangular swimming pool, which was fifty meters long, the water was flat and still, as green as a piece of jade. When a woman swims on the water, she looks like a beautiful goldfish, further enhanced by the slight ripples of the green waves, making her naturally feel extraordinarily moving and lovely. Moreover, there are also many vaguely protruding peaks hidden in the swimsuits, and trembling fleshy legs, which can make people intoxicated. Jun first dived into the water from the springboard, put her head on the surface of the water, and waved at me with her hand. I stood on the side and looked around, then patted my chest and jumped into the pool. Immersed in the water, I felt infinitely cool and comfortable, and my spirit was much more cheerful. Jun and I kicked our feet in the shallow water and swam as hard as we could towards the deep end of the pool. The two of us had a temporary race, and as a result, Jun's skills were much better than mine, so I ended up falling behind by more than a foot.

Here, there are absolutely no gender boundaries. Everyone is half-naked, and there are no classes. You can swim and play to your heart's content. Some people swim arm in arm in the water, while others whisper side by side by the pool, forgetting reality, forgetting ugliness. Only this moment is their time in a paradise of happiness.

There are several women who cannot swim. Although they are wearing fashionable swimsuits, they only play in the shallow water, stepping on the water, or being taught by male companions, giggling and laughing, showing off their romantic and ridiculous abilities to the fullest. At this moment, no one thinks about the economic depression of the world or the terror of the eve of war. Everyone wants to enjoy this moment of numbness and stimulation as much as possible!

The sound of water splashing, the sound of laughter, the sound of whistling, the sound of singing, all blended together around the pool. Swimming, watching, listening, whispering, you will never feel the fatigue of your limbs. Ah! That endless revelry!

It was already dusk, so we changed back into our clothes and followed everyone out of the gate of the swimming pool.

Doctor Deng Yuanhe's Trivial Talk on Lung Disease

Nutritional Issues for Improving Tuberculosis

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

Fourteen-Year-Old Elementary School Student Commits Suicide Out of Patriotic Concern

— Fang Jiu

In the past, there were cases of suicide due to patriotic concerns, such as Nanjing military officer Xu Fanting's suicide by cutting open his abdomen and Supervisory Yuan member Du Yi's suicide by drowning. Now, there is a report that Zhou Zixin, a fourteen-year-old elementary school student from Pucheng, committed suicide by swallowing nitric acid water. In this time of national crisis, when the enemy's iron hooves are about to trample our beautiful land, how can these solemn actions of suicide for the country not move people to tears?

While we express solemn respect for the patriotic suicides of military officer Xu Fanting and Supervisory Yuan member Du Yi, we do not think suicide is the solution. Although it is also a passive method, it stimulates the hearts of us living who have not yet died.

Elementary school students have particularly rich emotions. Therefore, they immediately cry when moved. They conceal nothing. Because of the increasing decline of the national situation, elementary school students want to go into the mountains to seek immortals and visit Daoists. This is because, after mastering magic, they can serve the country! However, this is a poor result of education, failing to guide elementary school students' patriotic concepts onto the right track. But what about the act of patriotic suicide by elementary school students? Strictly speaking, this is also a poor result of education.

We see that Zhou Zixin paid close attention to the national crisis on weekdays, and teachers and friends alike valued him. He often went to the library to read newspapers. What the newspapers published was, of course, worrying. Two sentences in the will of Zhou Zixin, this respectable and lovely child, moved me twelve hundred thousand times: " are forcing us so severely, and we are still fighting each other internally." This is what a fourteen-year-old child feels. Is it not the same as what we older youths, adults, and seniors feel?

I say that this elementary school student's patriotic suicide is, strictly speaking, also the result of poor education. This is because teachers only tell elementary school students about the tragic national situation on weekdays, but do not further encourage them and point out a correct path to save the country.

We should stand up solemnly and give the highest salute to this patriotic young student who committed suicide!

Village Scenery

— Peng

This time I went back to my hometown, I planned to stay at home for a long time. Indeed, I had already crawled enough on this long and difficult journey of life, passing the years like a snail. Since leaving home at the age of fifteen until now, I have not smelled the scent of grass and wheat from my hometown. I've only been mingling in the dusty metropolis, carrying the heavy burden of life.

Who knew that even before I had lived at home for ten days, I had returned to Shanghai. Everything in my hometown caused me so much pain! The impressions that remain in my mind still worry me.

I remember my hometown in my childhood, it was so full of life! Dense black smoke would rise from the chimneys of every house in the village. Houses were connected one after another, densely packed like beehives, so crowded that there were no small lanes for walking. In the early morning or at dusk, the village head was crowded with people; old people showed a kind smile, enthusiastically talking about ancient stories. Young people cheerfully talked about the scandalous affairs of who the village girls were sleeping with and who the young men were sleeping with in the villages around. Young women dressed like brides all year round—wearing red and green, proud of their beautiful youth, sitting together in groups of three or five, discussing trivial things. Children could be seen all day long on the threshing ground, playing hide-and-seek, and their innocent feelings flowed out from behind the rice stacks. The sounds of old women calling pigs and scolding chickens and ducks added to the commotion.

I have only been away from my hometown for five years, which is not a long time. How rapid are the changes in human affairs! It has become dilapidated like an old temple, and I can no longer hear joyful laughter. The resentment squeezed out by the heavy burden of life, like dark clouds, surrounds the village and fills the wilderness…

The day I returned home, my elderly uncle, leading my six-year-old nephew, excitedly ran to a small road four or five miles away to meet me.

Perhaps it was because he was too excited! Seeing this nephew who had not become rich, returning home for a while, made him fall deeper into the abyss of pain. Sitting under the flickering light of the vegetable oil lamp, everyone was silent—my uncle, aunt, brother, sister-in-law, and nephew, all hung their heads low, unable to say a word. This terrible silence, on the first day, wounded this traveler's heart that longed for his hometown.

Early the next morning, I said to my uncle: I want to go back to my own home and live there for a while. When my uncle heard this, he showed an even sadder face. He told me in a trembling voice: "Ah, do you think there is still a home? The walls have collapsed, and even the bricks have been taken away. Ah…" He sobbed, old tears streaming down his haggard face: "Ah! Do you still remember your aunt? This woman was no good. In the first year you left, she ran away with two men from other places, heartlessly leaving your brother…" He raised his weak hand and pointed at my aunt, meaning to ask her to respond to his words.

My aunt stood aside, also shedding tears. She wiped her eyes with her sleeve and said: "Hey! He's been dead for a long time, what's there to say!"

My uncle's village is only five or six miles away from my home, separated by a mountain. After crossing the mountain slope, my home can be seen. At this time, it was the stifling hot weather of deep summer, and the golden wheat seedlings in the fields were waving in the breeze. But the fields on both sides of the small road were so desolate, with only scattered rotten straw. Today, I finally believe that the world has really reached the point where there is land but no one to cultivate it.

When I arrived home, the sun had already set in the west, and the village seemed so deserted that there wasn't a single living creature. At the head of the village stood a middle-aged man as thin as a reed stick, feebly chopping withered trees. We looked at each other with surprised eyes. I didn't recognize him, and he didn't seem to know me either. After we passed him, he continued his work of chopping trees. I asked my elder brother, who is that person? He suddenly put on a strange expression and asked me in return: "What, don't you even recognize this person? He's Cai Laoer, who used to lead you around all day!"

"Oh! It's Cai Laoer!" A vivid memory revived in my mind. Cai Laoer, what a kind and optimistic man he used to be! But now, he… I dare not delve further into the memories of the past in my mind.

I hung my head low, stubbornly gritted my teeth, and rushed straight into my house, which had already fallen into disrepair.

After only staying there for one night, I returned to my uncle's house. A piece of the collar of my little jacket, stained with oil, was bitten off by rats while I slept at night, and my elder brother was even bitten on the finger.

To this day, I still carefully keep that tattered jacket with the collar eaten away. That is the only souvenir of my trip back to my hometown!

Page 20

Summer Flowers

— Liao Chuxiu

The most praised flower in summer is the lotus, but in this article, I don't want to talk about it, because I have another article specifically written about it.

The first flower since entering summer is the pomegranate. "The pomegranate flower shines brightly in May," its fiery scarlet color already symbolizes the heat of summer. Its strong burning flavor is like that of a southern girl, burning with fire-like enthusiasm in her healthy body. It is a force, a heart-piercing force. Under the bright summer sun, I don't know how many neurasthenic people dare not look directly at it.

Following the pomegranate flower is the plump gardenia. Han Tuizhi's poem "Banana leaves are large and gardenias are fat," this is a flower that symbolizes the pleasantness of summer. It carries the charm of a young woman. Although it does not seduce with its beauty, its plumpness truly gives people endless aftertaste. The gardenia is originally a subtropical flower. Therefore, "Wu Za Zu" says, "This flower is extremely abundant in Fujian and is cheap. It and jasmine and zhilan all grow regardless of the soil. It only gradually becomes valuable when it reaches Wu and Chu." The author of "Wu Za Zu" was a person from the Ming Dynasty, but his words still apply today. Among the hundreds of flowers, there are not many with six petals. The gardenia flower is one of the six-petaled ones. Therefore, there is a Wu song that says, "The gardenia flower has six petal heads," specially marking its characteristic—six petals—as a "starting point" for a love song. We have three or four gardenia plants in our house. My cousins and sisters all come to my house for temporary stays during the summer vacation. I am often entrusted by them to pick some newly opened gardenias early in the morning and soak them in water trays for them to wear in their hair when they comb their hair. Because we have our own, they always change to new ones two or three times a day. The young girls in the neighborhood occasionally beg for some, and soak them in water trays for them to wear in their hair for two or three days. In the evening, everyone gathers in the courtyard to enjoy the cool air. Sometimes it is very dark at night, and we cannot see the people opposite us, but only the fragrance of gardenias wafts in the wind, telling us that they are there.

"Banana leaves are large and gardenias are fat." Although the banana also blooms, that is limited to Fujian and Guangdong. Bananas in Jiangnan rarely bloom. Therefore, people say that the banana flower is the Yulan magnolia, but I don't know if that is true. However, although the banana does not bloom much, the canna blooms in summer. The beauty of the canna is different from the banana flower. Not only is the canna red and yellow, while the banana is white, but the appearance is also different. Chen Liuxian said, "The leaves of the canna tree are all like bananas but bloom less. They are bright red and gorgeous, with thousands of petals like mallets. They do not wither for several months. If you pick them and put them in a bottle and soak them in water, they can also last for a month or two." Indeed, if someone's garden has one or two cannas, then the long summer will not be lonely.

Tuberose, jasmine, and zhalan are all summer flowers. The Five Dynasties poem "Tuberose flowers in Hainan," then, the tuberose is undoubtedly a subtropical flower. Jasmine and zhalan can still be seen from time to time in Jiangnan, but they are very expensive between Yan and Zhao. These three flowers mostly win with fragrance, and their color and shape are nothing unusual.

Night-blooming jasmine is one of the main summer flowers. The ancients said, "This flower is conceived in the sun and blooms on the pillow. It is truly a lewd flower that delights the night, a seductive flower that lingers." Therefore, some people even say that the fragrance of the night-blooming jasmine must be mixed with the flesh, fragrance, and powder of women, then the marvel of it will be fully realized. I really have no reason to deny this.

White magnolia is not seen in ancient books, but it is currently very popular in Shanghai. Its fragrance is similar to that of night-blooming jasmine. If my feeling is correct, then it is more lewd than night-blooming jasmine, or perhaps it is popular in the city because of its lewdness.

When summer is about to end, the pure white tuberose goes on the market. This is a flower with a slight autumn feel. Its purity and its elegance are contrary to those of night-blooming jasmine and white magnolia. Now I already long for it, not to mention that what will come with it will be the clear and distant early autumn!

The Lost Smile

— Qiying

The whip of life drove me out of school. I regarded this society as the Garden of Eden, not facing reality and not caring about the unfortunate encounters of my kind being slaughtered. I indulged my character, arrogant of myself. Even in front of my superiors, I was willful, regardless of people's hatred or joy, doing what I wanted to do.

Then, some worldly friends older than me warned me? "××, you shouldn't be so naive!"

Yes, I shouldn't be so naive. Sometimes, when I heard such warnings from friends, my fragile and immature mind was hit hard. I vowed to deeply imprint this sentence in my mind and no longer knowingly violate it, but soon I returned to my original state.

When I was happy, I would forget everything. A bright and gentle sunlight seemed to envelop my fragile soul. In a group of friends, I learned to jump and laugh happily like a child, saying whatever I thought. Just as a word flowed out of my mouth, and my cheeks opened up when I laughed, a shadow of melancholy would cover my heart again. Because I may encounter malicious sarcasm from people. In their contemptuous sneers, I heard some words that would hurt my soul. I often exchanged a full heart of enthusiasm for people's cold faces.

In this way, I hesitated, I wavered, and I didn't know how to behave. I read many books on social science. I asked many friends about some of my difficult problems, but they all could not give me a satisfactory answer. I ran into walls on all sides, and I didn't have a close friend. Loneliness and sadness surrounded my heart.

During the day, I hid in a small and low room. I was doing something dishonorable, and I let painful memories and heavy coal smoke and heavy moisture torment my young life all day long. In the evening, unable to bear the silence, even if there was a heavy rain falling outside the window, I had to run out into the deserted street like a wild horse. Only when people were already intoxicated in the dreamland could I breathe a little fresh air!

The arrival of one season is also the passing of another season. My young man's senses had become so dull that they were almost like an idiot. All year round, on my dazed face, a dead silence could not raise a smile.

Finally, even a place to eat could not be found. A kind-hearted friend advised me:

"×× You have forgotten yourself, you have forgotten what kind of road fate has given you, you need to laugh, you need to laugh!"

He took me to a group of adult gentlemen, he told me: you get to know them, you don't have to worry about no way out; but you need to laugh. However, I can't laugh anymore. Even if I laugh, how lonely and miserable is that laugh!

Water Wheel (1)

— Li Ang

The eight mu of land gets water from the Dakunpi Port. The dyke is high and the water is shallow. It is really not easy to hoist water with a water wheel that requires five people to tread. The eight mu of land used to belong to three households in total: two mu to Shunfu, the crooked mouth, four mu to Uncle Shougen, and two mu to Qing Sheng's widow. When water was scarce, Uncle Shougen would always shout at the top of his voice to call people to tread the water wheel. His family farmed four mu of rice fields, so he was naturally anxious, and he hired a farmhand, so he didn't have to exert himself.

This morning, Qing Sheng's widow was moving her hairdressing tools to the threshing ground to fix her hair when Uncle Shougen walked over with his only son, who was born when he was forty-two years old: "You plan to dress up and go where?"

"Oh, Uncle Shougen, good morning. I'm going to town to buy some odds and ends." She held up her half-undone bun. The morning sun could not hide the gloom on her face. "It will be the anniversary of my family's… Mao Xiao's father's death in four days!"

Counting it, Qing Sheng, that poor and honest man, had been dead for three years. Mao Xiao was seven years old when he cried while holding the bamboo pole and memorial tablet for his father. He is ten years old this year, but he is so thin and small. His nose always sounds like he has a cold, and you can't pinch off an ounce or two of meat from his face. Old Mr. Mei Tang from Dong Village diagnosed him as having exhaustion from lack of male vitality. No one in the village likes him. Qing Sheng's widow always cries for him, sometimes crying for half a day at Qing Sheng's grave. But no one gives her sympathetic pity. Uncle Shougen didn't care about Qing Sheng's anniversary at all. He just warned:

"You know the eight mu of land needs water wheeling, today, today!"

"Oh, oh, but… I'll just call my Mao Xiao to come, I still have to go to the Earth God Temple to burn paper…" Uncle Shougen's only son in his arms cried. He seemed very impatient to hear her talk about inauspicious dead people. He "hmphed" at her, coaxing his child, while turning around and walking towards the back door of Shunfu's, the crooked mouth's, house, muttering: "Water wheeling always sends children to do it. Others always take advantage of you. Is it enough for your two mu of land to send a little sick ghost…" These words, these words… (To be continued)

Star Film Company Second Studio Holds Major Rehearsal

Ouyang Yuqian and Ying Yunwei Direct, Most of the Second Studio's Actors Perform

On July 17th, the Star Film Company's Second Studio convened film crew members who had not yet worked together for a rehearsal. The main principle of this rehearsal was to have this group of new people on the same line of work gain an initial understanding and connection with each other before the start of the Second Studio's two opening productions: Ying Yunwei's "United Hearts in Life and Death" and Ouyang Yuqian's "Qingming Season". The rehearsal was divided into two groups. The first group was directed by Ouyang Yuqian, with actresses Li Minghui, Li Lilian, Wang Feijuan, Zhang Dieping, Lu Luming, and others, and male actors Xie Jingbo, Li Qing, Tian Chen, and others. The second group was directed by Ying Yunwei, with actresses Gong Qiuxia, Ying Yin, Hu Rongrong, and others, and male actors Wang Ruoxi, Liu Mang, Yao Ping, and others. On the technical side, the cinematographer for the first group was Yan Bingheng, and the sound engineers were the He Zhaohuang and Zhaozhang brothers. The cinematographer for the second group was Wu Yin Xian, and the sound engineer was Lu Yinkeng. This rehearsal was no different from an actual film shoot, except that the directors only gave the actors a few interesting lines of dialogue and a brief plot outline based on their personalities, but they still performed as if it were real. Those who could sing, like Li Minghui, Gong Qiuxia, and Ying Yin, sang a few songs, and the performances of those burly men like Li Qing also included fist fights. The performance started at 2:00 PM and ended at 8:00 PM.

The Most Complete Song Selection: Collection of Voices of China to be Published Soon

The Collection of Voices of China (Selection of Heroic Songs) is compiled by Zhou Weishi, mainly selected by Li Gongpu, and proofread by Sun Shiyi. The song collection gathers the most recent songs that reflect reality and awaken the masses. There are over 110 songs in total. This collection does not contain decadent, sentimental tunes, nor moans of personal private life, nor deceptive sermons that anesthetize people. What you will find here is the roar of a lion after awakening, and the long howl of breaking free from shackles. For the convenience of practical application, the entire collection divides the songs into seven parts: national, youth, workers and peasants, soldiers, women, children, and voices of the times, and includes the sheet music for national anthems of various countries for research purposes. At the same time, in order to enable the public to read numbered musical notation and know how to sing, the editor has also written out some of the most common and frequently used rules in a very accessible way, so that those who have read it can self-study singing methods. The collection is also arranged in a very neat format, correcting all the mistakes found in those boring so-called selections and collections. This is currently the most complete song collection, and also an extremely needed song collection during the high tide of the national salvation movement. In order to promote the "Voices of National Salvation," each copy is sold for only 15 cents, and will be published before the end of the month, distributed by Reading Life Publishing House.

Carole Lombard and Fredric March Co-Star in "Nothing Sacred"

Guangming Screening

Disney Wins Last Year's Top Cartoon Award

— Lai

The famous cartoon artist Walt Disney was awarded the 1936 Academy of Arts and Sciences Award for his masterpiece "Three Orphan Kittens" from last year. This cartoon film is considered the best work of 1935.

"Three Orphan Kittens" is a color cartoon that tells the story of two kittens making mischief in a house, inciting a mouse to create a commotion on the piano out of hatred for a cook.

Disney is truly a great filmmaker; including this time, he has received the award four times.

The 1932 award-winning work was "Flowers and Trees."

The 1933 award-winner was "Three Little Pigs."

The 1934 award-winner was "The Tortoise and the Hare."

The "Three Little Pigs" and other cartoons were screened around the world and were very popular, with audiences unanimously praising his drawing skills.

The famous filmmaker and manager Kodak praised him in fifteen words: "He is a rare and great contributor to the film industry."

Finally, here's another piece of news for readers: Disney has left United Artists and joined RKO Pictures.

His new work "Clubhouse Sketches" is already in production, assisted by the new female cartoon writer Annie Manlin.
